# 500 ChatGPT Prompts for Business Growth

**The Ultimate AI Prompt Library for Entrepreneurs, Marketers, and Business Builders**

Last Updated: May 2026 · 500 Prompts · 8 Categories

---

## 1. Marketing Prompts (80 Prompts)

Prompts for audience research, campaign planning, social media strategy, email marketing, SEO, paid ads, brand positioning, and marketing analytics.

### 1.1 Full Audience Persona Builder
**Use case:** Create detailed, data-backed buyer personas for your product or service
**Best for:** Founders, marketers, product managers

Act as a seasoned market researcher specializing in B2B and B2C audience analysis. Build a comprehensive buyer persona for my business.

Start by asking me these five questions one at a time:
1. What product or service do you sell?
2. Who are your current best customers (demographics, job titles, industries)?
3. What specific problem does your product solve?
4. Who are your top 3 competitors?
5. What objection do prospects most commonly raise?

Once I answer all five, create a detailed persona that includes: demographic profile, psychographic profile (values, fears, aspirations), a day-in-the-life narrative, buying triggers, information sources they trust, common objections with rebuttals, preferred communication channels, and a one-sentence summary of how to market to this persona effectively.

**Expected output:** A 500-700 word comprehensive buyer persona document ready for team sharing
**Pro tip:** Run this for each of your top 3 customer segments, then compare for patterns across segments

### 1.2 Multi-Channel Campaign Architect
**Use case:** Design a coordinated marketing campaign across 5+ channels
**Best for:** Marketing managers, business owners

Act as a digital marketing strategist with 15 years of experience launching integrated campaigns for B2B and B2C companies. I need you to architect a complete multi-channel campaign.

Here is my campaign context:
- **Product/offer:** [product or service being promoted]
- **Target audience:** [specific audience description]
- **Campaign goal:** [e.g., generate 100 leads, sell 50 units, get 1,000 signups]
- **Timeline:** [campaign duration in days or weeks]
- **Budget:** [budget description from minimal to specific amount]
- **Available channels:** [list 3-5 channels you can use]

Design a campaign where each channel has a specific role: awareness channel, consideration channel, conversion channel, and retention channel. For each channel, provide the specific content or asset needed, the messaging angle tailored to that platform, the call-to-action, posting schedule with dates, and explicit connection to other channels. Then create a campaign timeline showing content flow between channels with dependencies highlighted.

**Expected output:** A complete campaign brief with channel-by-channel breakdown and visual timeline
**Pro tip:** After generating, ask ChatGPT to create a detailed content calendar from this plan

### 1.3 Value Proposition Refiner
**Use case:** Sharpen and test your unique value proposition using structured analysis
**Best for:** Founders, product marketers

Apply constraint-based and reverse engineering techniques to refine my value proposition. Follow these steps precisely.

Step 1 — Question Phase: Ask me these four questions one at a time: (a) What does your product or service do? (b) Who specifically is it for? (c) What is the single biggest result your customers achieve? (d) Why is that result difficult to achieve without you?

Step 2 — Analysis Phase: Once I answer all four, analyze my responses for clarity (is it instantly understandable?), specificity (are there concrete outcomes?), differentiation (does it separate from competitors?), and emotional resonance (does it tap into a real desire or fear?).

Step 3 — Generation Phase: Create 5 variations of my value proposition using these frameworks: "We help [audience] achieve [outcome] by [mechanism]", "Stop [pain point] and start [desired outcome] with [product]", "The [category] for [audience] who want [benefit] without [sacrifice]", "From [current state] to [desired state]", and "[Audience]'s secret to [outcome]".

Step 4 — Recommendation: Score each variation on Clarity (1-10), Memorability (1-10), and Differentiation (1-10), then recommend the winner with detailed reasoning.

**Expected output:** 5 value proposition variations with scores and a recommended winner with rationale
**Pro tip:** Test your winning value proposition by running the A/B Split Test Designer prompt later in this pack

### 1.4 SEO Content Cluster Strategy
**Use case:** Build a topical authority strategy with pillar pages and cluster content
**Best for:** Content marketers, SEO specialists

Act as an SEO strategist who has built content programs driving millions of organic visits. I need a complete topical authority content cluster strategy.

My business: [describe your business and target keywords]
My website: [your URL]
My primary keyword focus: [main keyword you want to rank for]

Follow this chain-of-thought process: First, analyze my primary keyword for search intent (informational, commercial, transactional, navigational) and difficulty. Second, identify 5-8 subtopics (pillar page candidates) that surround my primary keyword. For each subtopic, specify the pillar page keyword, 5-8 cluster article topics with search intent for each, recommended content format (listicle, guide, comparison, tutorial, case study), and internal linking structure. Third, recommend a content publishing calendar showing which pieces to publish first based on quick wins versus long-term authority building. Fourth, suggest schema markup types for each pillar page. Fifth, provide 3 link-building strategies specific to my industry.

**Expected output:** A complete content cluster strategy document with publishing sequence and link-building tactics
**Pro tip:** Export this to a spreadsheet and track publishing dates, word counts, and rankings monthly

### 1.5 Viral Social Media Hook Generator
**Use case:** Create scroll-stopping hooks for social media posts across platforms
**Best for:** Social media managers, content creators

You are a viral content strategist who has studied 10,000+ high-performing social media posts across Instagram, TikTok, LinkedIn, and Twitter. Your expertise is crafting hooks that stop the scroll and drive engagement.

I need hooks for [topic/industry/niche] targeting [specific audience].

Apply this constraint-based framework: Use one of these 9 hook patterns for each hook:
1. The Curiosity Gap: "I tried [method] for [timeframe] and [unexpected result]"
2. The Bold Statement: "Everything you know about [topic] is wrong"
3. The Specific Number: "[Number] ways to [achieve outcome] without [pain point]"
4. The Direct Address: "If you are [audience characteristic], stop doing [behavior]"
5. The Story Opener: "I ignored [advice] for [timeframe]. Here is what happened."
6. The Question: "Why do [audience] keep [painful activity] when [solution exists]?"
7. The Contrast: "Most [audience] do X. Smart [audience] do Y."
8. The Authority Play: "After analyzing [data point], I discovered [insight]"
9. The Emotional Trigger: "The [emotion] truth about [topic] that no one talks about"

Each hook must be under 15 words, include a specific concrete element, and not be clickbait. Generate 20 hooks total — 5 for each platform: LinkedIn, Twitter, Instagram, TikTok.

**Expected output:** 20 platform-specific hooks with explanations of why each works for that audience
**Pro tip:** A/B test the weakest hook against the strongest to measure the real performance gap

### 1.6 Google Ads Copy Suite
**Use case:** Write complete Google Ads campaigns with headlines, descriptions, and extensions
**Best for:** PPC specialists, business owners running search ads

Act as a Google Ads copywriter who has managed over $5M in ad spend across e-commerce, SaaS, and local service businesses. I need a complete ad copy suite for my campaign.

Campaign details: Product/service being advertised, target keywords, target audience, top 3 unique selling points, specific offer or promotion, and landing page goal.

For each keyword group (up to 3 groups), generate Responsive Search Ads with 5 headlines using different angles (benefit-driven, problem-aware, curiosity, social proof, urgency), 5 backup headlines with different CTAs, and 3 descriptions that each include a benefit, address an objection, and end with a CTA. Then provide ad extensions: 5 sitelinks with description lines, 3 callout extensions, and 1 structured snippet with 5 values. Finally, suggest 10+ negative keywords to exclude irrelevant traffic.

**Expected output:** Complete Google Ads copy with RSAs and extensions for up to 3 keyword groups
**Pro tip:** After generating, ask ChatGPT to create a keyword match-type strategy (exact, phrase, broad modified)

### 1.7 Email Nurture Sequence Builder
**Use case:** Design a multi-email nurture sequence that converts leads into customers
**Best for:** Email marketers, sales teams

Apply persona framing and chain-of-thought to build an 8-email nurture sequence. First, I will tell you about my business and audience, then you build the sequence step by step.

Business context: What I sell, target customer persona, lead magnet or opt-in offer, typical sales cycle length, and primary goal of this sequence (book a call, make a sale, drive trial, etc.).

Now build these emails:
1. **Deliverable:** Deliver the promised value + set expectations. Warm and helpful, not salesy.
2. **Social Proof:** Share a customer success story using the before/after/bridge narrative.
3. **Problem Deepener:** Expand on the problem using data showing the cost of inaction.
4. **Solution Introduction:** Introduce your product as the natural solution. Benefits over features.
5. **Objection Handler:** Address the top 3 objections using the feel-felt-found framework.
6. **Social Proof 2:** Share a second case study from a different use case or industry segment.
7. **Urgency:** Create legitimate urgency — limited-time bonus, price increase, or capacity constraint.
8. **Final Push:** Last-chance email summarizing the transformation with a clear next step.

For each email provide: subject line (3 options), preview text, body copy, CTA button text, and optimal send day/time recommendation.

**Expected output:** Complete 8-email nurture sequence with all elements ready for your email platform
**Pro tip:** After building the sequence, ask ChatGPT to write 3 A/B test subject lines for each email

### 1.8 Competitive Positioning Matrix
**Use case:** Map your competitive landscape and find positioning gaps
**Best for:** Founders, product marketers, strategists

Act as a competitive intelligence analyst using a structured framework to map market positioning. Follow this analysis framework step by step.

Step 1 — Competitive Feature Matrix: Create a table with features as rows and companies (mine + competitors) as columns. Include these attribute categories: core functionality, pricing model, target audience size, key integrations, customer support level, and unique differentiators.

Step 2 — Perceptual Map: Define two axes that matter most to our customers (such as Price vs. Quality or Simple vs. Powerful). Place each competitor on this 2x2 grid and identify occupied positions, crowded positions, and empty opportunity zones.

Step 3 — Positioning Gap Analysis: For each empty position, evaluate whether it is a viable market opportunity, whether our product naturally fits, what it would take to claim that position, and the estimated market size.

Step 4 — Messaging Battle Cards: For each top 3 competitor, create a battle card with their likely positioning statement, our counter-positioning argument, 3 proof points supporting our advantage, and one honest concession where they are stronger.

Step 5 — Recommended Positioning Strategy: Recommend which position we should claim, a draft positioning statement, and 3 key messages to reinforce this position.

**Expected output:** Complete competitive analysis with positioning recommendations and battle cards
**Pro tip:** Update this matrix quarterly — competitive landscapes shift fast in most industries

### 1.9 Customer Interview Question Bank
**Use case:** Design customer discovery or validation interviews that reveal real insights
**Best for:** Founders, product managers, UX researchers

You are a user research specialist trained in the Mom Test methodology and Jobs-to-be-Done framework. I need a structured 45-minute customer interview guide.

My product or service: [what you offer or plan to build]
Target interviewee profile: [who you want to interview]
Research goals: [specific unknowns you want to learn]

Design the guide in these phases. Phase 1 — Rapport and Context (5 minutes): Warm-up questions that establish trust and get the person talking naturally. Avoid leading questions about your product. Phase 2 — Problem Exploration (12 minutes): Questions uncovering how they currently handle the problem area, what they have tried before, what frustrates them, what "good enough" looks like, and how much this problem costs them in time, money, or emotion. Phase 3 — Solution Validation (10 minutes): Questions to test your solution concept WITHOUT biasing the response. Phase 4 — Priority and Willingness to Pay (8 minutes): Questions assessing how important this problem is compared to others, what they have spent solving it, and what a reasonable price point would be. Phase 5 — Wrap-up (5 minutes): Questions that surface unexpected insights.

For each phase provide: 5-8 specific questions, follow-up probes to dig deeper, signs you are getting a real answer versus a polite answer, and red flags indicating the conversation is off-track.

**Expected output:** Complete 45-minute interview guide with questions, probes, and red flags for each phase
**Pro tip:** Record interviews with permission and use ChatGPT afterward to analyze transcripts for patterns

### 1.10 Launch Sequence Generator
**Use case:** Plan a multi-phase product launch with coordinated marketing activities
**Best for:** Product marketers, founders

Act as a launch strategist who has overseen 50+ product launches from $5K to $5M. I need a complete launch sequence using the See-Think-Do-Care framework.

Product details: name, type (digital, physical, SaaS, service, course), price point, ideal customer description, key benefit in one sentence, launch timeline, and current audience size (email list, followers, etc.).

Design three phases. Pre-Launch Phase: Activities to build anticipation including teaser content, lead magnet or free value, social proof collection, waitlist or early access mechanics, and referral or affiliate recruitment. Launch Phase: Day-by-day activities for launch week from announcement through social proof, feature deep-dive, objection handling, urgency push, final call, and extended period. Post-Launch Phase: Onboarding sequence, upsell or cross-sell opportunities, referral program activation, testimonial request system, and content recycling.

For each phase specify: specific assets needed, distribution channels, success metrics or KPIs, and budget allocation recommendations.

**Expected output:** Complete launch plan with daily activities across all three phases
**Pro tip:** After planning, use the Content Creation section prompts later in this pack to write each piece of launch content

### 1.11 Marketing KPI Dashboard Builder
**Use case:** Define the marketing metrics that actually matter for your specific business
**Best for:** Marketing managers, business owners

Apply reverse engineering to build a marketing KPI dashboard from the ground up. Start with this end goal: I want to achieve [specific business outcome]. Now work backward with me.

Step 1 — North Star Metric: What single metric best predicts long-term success for my business model? Recommend one with rationale. Step 2 — Input Metrics: What 5-8 leading indicators drive the North Star? For each one define it precisely, explain why it matters, suggest a target value, and recommend measurement frequency. Step 3 — Channel-Level Metrics: For each marketing channel I use, identify the top 3 metrics to track, benchmark ranges for my industry, and actionable thresholds for when to increase investment versus cut losses. Step 4 — Dashboard Design: Create a dashboard layout with a top section showing the North Star plus 3 key input metrics, a middle section for channel performance, and a bottom section for health metrics (CAC, LTV, ROAS, churn). For each metric specify the definition, formula, data source, and target range.

**Expected output:** Complete KPI framework with dashboard layout and metric definitions ready to build
**Pro tip:** Create this dashboard in Google Data Studio or your analytics tool with the exact metrics defined here

### 1.12 Reddit Marketing Playbook
**Use case:** Build a non-spammy Reddit presence that drives traffic and authority
**Best for:** Founders, growth marketers

Act as a Reddit marketing veteran who has built multiple brands to six-figure revenue primarily through Reddit traffic. Create a subreddit-specific marketing playbook.

My business: [describe your business]
Target audience interests: [what they care about]
Subreddits they frequent: [list specific subreddits]
My product URL: [your website or offer]

Create these sections. Audience Mapping: For each subreddit, identify the community culture (tone, inside jokes, pet peeves), what content format performs best, posting rules and restrictions, peak activity times, and the specific problems discussed that your product addresses. Value-First Content Strategy: 5 content ideas per subreddit that provide genuine value before mentioning your product. The Soft Pitch Technique: How to naturally introduce your product when relevant using framing templates, contextual sharing, and AMA strategy. Engagement Guidelines: Daily routine with time allocation, comment quality standards, the 9-to-1 ratio rule (9 value comments for every 1 self-promotion), and reputation building timeline.

**Expected output:** Complete subreddit-by-subreddit marketing playbook with content ideas and posting guidelines
**Pro tip:** Use Reddit's Top of Past Month filter to study what content resonates in your target subreddits before posting

### 1.13 Video Marketing Script Outliner
**Use case:** Structure compelling video content for YouTube, TikTok, or Instagram Reels
**Best for:** Content creators, video marketers

You are a video script consultant who has helped creators grow channels from zero to millions of views. I need a complete video structure for my content.

Video details: platform, topic, target audience, goal (awareness, engagement, conversion, education), length target, and brand voice (professional, casual, educational, entertaining).

Create a script outline using these components. Hook (first 3-15 seconds depending on platform): 3 hook options using pattern interrupt, curiosity gap, direct problem statement, or bold promise. Body Structure: Organize content using one of these structures — Problem-Solution-Benefit, Before-After-Bridge, List or Numbered Format, Storytelling Arc, or Educational Framework. For each segment provide a timestamp marker, key talking points, visual or onscreen element suggestions, and transition to the next segment. Call to Action: 3 options for engagement (comment or like), subscription or follow, or external action (link in bio, website visit). Description and Metadata: Optimized title (3 options with keywords), description template, hashtag strategy, and thumbnail concept suggestions.

**Expected output:** Complete video script outline with hooks, body, CTA, and metadata recommendations
**Pro tip:** After scripting, use the Copywriting section prompts to refine your script for retention and impact

### 1.14 Webinar and Presentation Script
**Use case:** Write a compelling webinar or live presentation script from opening to close
**Best for:** Sales teams, educators, thought leaders

Act as a presentation coach who has trained TEDx speakers and Fortune 500 executives. I need a complete script for a live presentation.

Presentation details: topic, title, audience, total duration, format (live webinar, recorded, in-person keynote), main outcome for attendees, and what you are selling or offering.

Write a complete script following this structure. Opening (first 3 minutes): Hook using story, statistic, question, or provocative statement. Context-setting for why this topic matters NOW. Agenda preview of what they will learn. Credibility statement in 2 sentences max. Content Delivery (70% of time): Divide into 3-4 segments. For each segment provide a key teaching point, supporting evidence, audience engagement element, visual slide suggestion, and transition. Application or Workshop Segment: Guided exercise with instructions, time allocation, example output, and debrief questions. Q and A Preparation: Anticipate 10 likely questions with prepared answers and bridges back to your message. Closing (last 5 minutes): Summary of key takeaways, specific time-bound call to action, open loop close connecting back to the opening hook, and thank you with next steps.

**Expected output:** Full presentation script with timing, slide suggestions, and Q and A preparation
**Pro tip:** After writing, rehearse with ChatGPT in role-play mode having it act as your audience asking tough questions

### 1.15 Facebook Ad Copy Generator
**Use case:** Write high-converting Facebook and Instagram ad copy for different audience segments
**Best for:** Social media advertisers, business owners

Act as a direct-response copywriter who specializes in Facebook and Instagram ads. I need ad copy for three audience segments using the Attention-Interest-Desire-Action formula.

Campaign details: product or service, target audience interests, offer, primary objective (sales, leads, traffic, engagement), landing page URL, and ad creative description.

Generate three complete ad sets. Primary Ad Set (cold audience): Primary text with hook, problem, solution, social proof, and CTA. Headline that is benefit-driven or curiosity-based. Description with supporting benefit. Best CTA button. Retargeting Ad Set (warm audience): Acknowledgment hook, objection address using the top reason people do not buy, social proof injection with specific testimonial or number, low-friction offer, and reduced commitment language CTA. Lookalike Ad Set (expanded cold audience): Broader positioning focusing on category not specific solution, education-first hook, authority-building copy, and risk reversal with guarantee or money-back.

For every ad include 3 headline options with character counts and a brief rationale for why this angle works for the audience type.

**Expected output:** 3 complete ad sets (cold, warm, retargeting) with full copy and strategic rationale
**Pro tip:** Run the primary and retargeting sets simultaneously — retargeting ads consistently outperform cold for most businesses

### 1.16 Influencer Outreach Template Set
**Use case:** Craft outreach messages that get influencers to respond and collaborate
**Best for:** Growth marketers, brand managers

You are a partnership marketing expert who has secured 200+ influencer collaborations. I need a set of outreach templates that actually get responses.

My brand: [name and description] | My product: [what you want influencers to promote] | Offer to influencer: [payment, free product, affiliate commission, cross-promotion] | Target influencer type: [micro, macro, nano and their niche] | What makes my brand unique: [why they would want to work with us]

Create 4 outreach templates. Template 1 — Cold DM or Email (No Prior Connection): Warm opening referencing specific content they created. Why I reached out to THEM specifically. The value proposition for them. Low-friction ask. Under 150 words. Template 2 — Warm Outreach (They Follow or Engage With Us): Acknowledge existing connection. Build on shared interest. Propose specific collaboration idea tailored to their content style. Template 3 — Follow-up (No Response After 5 Days): Reference first message without guilt-tripping. Add one new piece of value. Make it easy to say yes. Option to decline gracefully. Template 4 — Partnership Confirmation and Brief: Congratulatory tone. Campaign overview in bullet points. Deliverables list with deadlines. Brand guidelines summary. Payment terms. Asset links.

For each template include: best sending time or channel, personalization tips, subject line (for email), and how to track response rates.

**Expected output:** 4 complete outreach templates with personalization guidance for each scenario
**Pro tip:** Personalize the first 2 sentences of every outreach — influencers can spot mass emails instantly

### 1.17 Customer Testimonial and Case Study Framework
**Use case:** Systematically collect and structure customer success stories
**Best for:** Marketing teams, customer success managers

Act as a case study writer who has produced 100+ customer stories for B2B and B2C companies. I need a systematic approach to collecting and writing testimonials and case studies.

My product or service: [what you sell]
My customer profile: [who buys from you]
The transformation I deliver: [the outcome customers achieve]

Create a complete system. Collection Strategy: When and how to ask for testimonials including timing triggers (immediately after success milestone, renewal, positive support interaction), ask methods (in-app prompt, email sequence, personal outreach), and incentive structure. Questionnaire for Customers: 10 interview questions organized by the STAR framework (Situation, Task, Action, Result) plus bonus questions about the moment they realized it was working and what almost held them back. Testimonial Formats: Short quote (1-2 sentences for homepage), medium testimonial (3-5 sentences for landing pages), long-form case study (500-1000 words with data), video testimonial script outline, and social media testimonial graphic text. Case Study Template: Complete structure including result-driven title, executive summary, the challenge (before state), the solution, the results with specific numbers, customer quote, and visual asset suggestions.

**Expected output:** Complete testimonial system with collection strategy, interview questions, and templates
**Pro tip:** Ask for testimonials immediately after a customer says something positive in support or a check-in call

### 1.18 Content Distribution Checklist
**Use case:** Maximize reach for every piece of content you create with zero paid budget
**Best for:** Content marketers, founders doing their own marketing

Apply constraint-based thinking to build a content distribution checklist with the constraint being zero paid budget.

Here is the content: [blog post, video, podcast, infographic, or other format]
Topic: [content topic]
Target audience: [who should see this]
Primary platform: [where this content lives permanently]

Create a distribution checklist organized by time horizon. Day 1 — Launch Blitz on Own Channels: Email list with subject line, preview text, send time, and segment. Social media per platform with optimal posting time, native format, hashtag strategy, and tagging relevant people. Website placement, related posts linking, and notification setup. Community sharing in relevant Slack, Discord, Facebook groups, and LinkedIn groups. Day 2-3 — Organic Amplification: Repurpose content into 5+ formats: tweet thread, LinkedIn carousel, Instagram story, short video clip, quote graphic. Answer related questions on Quora, Reddit, and LinkedIn comments. Reach out to 5 people mentioned or quoted, 3 complementary creators for cross-promotion, and collaborators. Day 4-7 — Long-Tail Distribution: SEO optimization with new internal links and refreshed metadata. Content syndication on Medium, LinkedIn Articles, and industry publications. Roundup submissions to newsletters and resource pages. Set evergreen update reminder.

**Expected output:** Complete content distribution checklist with timeline and tracking framework
**Pro tip:** Spend 60% of your time on distribution and 40% on creation — most people invert this ratio

### 1.19 Brand Voice and Tone Guide Generator
**Use case:** Define and document your brand's unique voice and tone across all contexts
**Best for:** Founders, marketing teams creating brand guidelines

Act as a brand strategist who has developed voice and tone guides for startups and enterprises. Help me define my brand's voice and create a documented guide.

My brand: [name] | My industry: [industry] | Target audience: [who I am speaking to] | Brand personality in 3 words: [adjectives] | Competitors: [2-3 main ones]

Step 1 — Voice Dimensions Assessment: Rate your brand on these spectrums from 1 to 5: Formal vs Casual, Serious vs Playful, Respectful vs Irreverent, Factual vs Emotional, Expert vs Peer, Direct vs Subtle, Concise vs Descriptive. Based on the ratings, synthesize a voice archetype such as The Approachable Expert or The Bold Disruptor. Step 2 — Voice Characteristics: Define 4 voice characteristics with a description, examples of what TO do, examples of what NOT to do, and how each characteristic shows up in different contexts. Step 3 — Tone Spectrum: Create a tone matrix showing how the voice adapts across happy moments, serious situations, educational contexts, sales messaging, and support interactions. Step 4 — Vocabulary and Grammar: Word choice guidelines including words we use, words we avoid with alternatives, grammar rules, and formatting preferences. Step 5 — Application Examples: Show the voice in action across a homepage hero, social media post, error message, email newsletter, and sales page.

**Expected output:** Complete brand voice and tone guide document ready to share with your team
**Pro tip:** Print this guide and keep it visible for anyone creating content for your brand

### 1.20 Pinterest SEO Strategy
**Use case:** Optimize Pinterest presence for long-term organic traffic
**Best for:** Visual brands, e-commerce, bloggers

Act as a Pinterest strategist who has driven millions of monthly viewers through Pinterest SEO. I need a complete optimization strategy.

My website: [URL] | My niche: [industry or topic] | Target keywords: [what people search for] | Current Pinterest presence: [existing account status]

Design a Pinterest growth strategy with these components. Keyword Research: How to find high-volume low-competition keywords using Pinterest guided search. Identify 10 head keywords (high volume, competitive), 20 body keywords (moderate volume and competition), and 30 long-tail keywords (lower volume but high intent). For each keyword provide search volume indicator, competition level, and content idea. Pin Design and SEO: Title formula using keyword plus benefit. Description template with keyword-rich first 2 lines. Board placement strategy. Hashtag strategy. Image specifications including vertical 2:3 ratio and text overlay best practices. Publishing Strategy: Posting frequency minimum for growth, optimal scheduling times, batching system for creating 30 pins in one session, and fresh pin versus repin ratio. Growth Tactics: Group board strategy, collaborative board approach, viral pin pattern analysis, Idea Pin strategy, and community engagement.

**Expected output:** Complete Pinterest SEO strategy with keyword research and content creation plan
**Pro tip:** Pinterest acts as a visual search engine — treat your pin descriptions like SEO metadata, not social captions

### 1.21 Marketing Experiment Design Canvas
**Use case:** Design structured marketing experiments with clear hypotheses and success criteria
**Best for:** Growth marketers, data-driven founders

Act as a growth marketing scientist. I need to design a structured marketing experiment to validate an approach before scaling it.

My business: [describe] | The idea I want to test: [specific marketing approach or channel] | Target metric to improve: [conversion rate, CTR, signups, engagement] | Current baseline: [current value of that metric] | Available resources: [budget, time, tools] | Risk tolerance: [how much you can invest before needing results]

Design a complete marketing experiment. Hypothesis Statement: Structure it as "If we [specific change], then [specific metric] will change by [predictable amount], because [logical reasoning]." Experiment Design: Test type (A/B test, before/after, multivariate, split test), control group description, variable group description, sample size required for statistical significance, duration accounting for day-of-week variation, and success criteria with minimum detectable effect. Implementation Plan: Setup steps, tracking implementation, quality assurance checklist, and launch procedure. Monitoring Rules: Go/no-go checkpoints, early stopping rules, and external factors to track. Analysis Framework: How to analyze results, confounding variables, and decision framework for whether to scale, iterate, or kill the experiment.

**Expected output:** Complete experiment design document with hypothesis, setup, and decision framework
**Pro tip:** Run experiments for a minimum of 7 days to capture full weekly cycles — shorter tests give misleading results

### 1.22 Channel Selection and Prioritization Matrix
**Use case:** Decide which marketing channels to invest in based on your specific situation
**Best for:** Founders, marketing leaders with limited resources

Apply constraint-based analysis to help me choose where to focus my marketing efforts given limited time and budget.

My business: [describe] | Target audience: [who you sell to] | Price point: [price] | 90-day growth goal: [specific metric and target] | Weekly hours for marketing: [hours available] | Monthly budget: [amount] | Channels already tried: [what you have tested and results]

Evaluate these channels for my specific situation: SEO, Content Marketing, Email Marketing, Social Media (organic), Paid Social, Google Ads, Influencer Marketing, Partnerships, Community Building, PR, Direct Sales, Events, Webinars. For each channel analyze: expected time to first result, estimated effort to launch, ongoing maintenance hours, potential reach, conversion intent, cost structure, our current strength (1-10), and competitor presence.

Create a 2x2 prioritization matrix with Impact on the X-axis and Effort on the Y-axis. Place each channel in one of four quadrants: Quick Wins (high impact, low effort), Major Projects (high impact, high effort), Fill-Ins (low impact, low effort), and Avoid (low impact, high effort). Recommend the top 3 channels to focus on now with a phased rollout plan and success milestones.

**Expected output:** Prioritized channel matrix with phased implementation plan and success milestones
**Pro tip:** Focus on 1-2 channels at a time until they produce consistent results before adding more

### 1.23 Customer Journey Map Creator
**Use case:** Map the complete customer journey from awareness to advocacy
**Best for:** Marketing teams, product managers, UX designers

Act as a customer experience strategist. I need to map my customer's complete journey so I can identify gaps and opportunities at every stage.

My business: [describe] | Product or service: [what customers buy] | Customer persona: [brief description] | Typical purchase cycle: [how long from awareness to purchase]

Create a comprehensive journey map with 6 stages. Stage 1 — Awareness: How customers first discover us. Touchpoints, customer questions, emotional state, current experience, and gap analysis. Stage 2 — Consideration: How they evaluate us. Touchpoints (website, reviews, comparisons), questions, emotional state, and gaps. Stage 3 — Decision or Purchase: The conversion moment. Touchpoints (checkout, signup, sales call), friction points, and emotional state. Stage 4 — Onboarding or Activation: First experience after purchase. Touchpoints (welcome email, setup flow), drop-off risks. Stage 5 — Retention and Ongoing Use: Regular usage pattern. Touchpoints (product, support, community). Opportunities to increase stickiness. Stage 6 — Advocacy: Customers become promoters. Touchpoints (referral program, reviews). What triggers advocacy.

For each stage provide a moment of truth (the single most influential interaction), metrics to track, and 3 improvement ideas prioritized by effort versus impact.

**Expected output:** Complete customer journey map with gap analysis for all 6 stages
**Pro tip:** Interview 5 customers and map their ACTUAL journey — the gaps between your assumptions and their reality will surprise you

### 1.24 Podcast Outreach and Pitch Kit
**Use case:** Get yourself or your founder featured on relevant podcasts
**Best for:** Founders, thought leaders building authority

Act as a PR and podcast booking agent who has secured 500+ podcast appearances. I need a complete podcast outreach system.

My profile: [who you are and your expertise] | Topics of expertise: [what you can speak about] | Target podcasts: [ideal podcast description] | Current audience: [follower count, email list size, traffic] | Product or service: [what you sell]

Create a podcast outreach system. Podcast Selection Criteria: How to identify the right podcasts based on relevance, engagement metrics, host style, listener count threshold, and past guest quality. Pitch Email Templates: Template A for cold pitch to podcasts you have listened to with personalized opener, specific topic pitch, credentials in one line, sample recording link, and low-friction next step. Template B for referral-based pitch with warm introduction. Template C for follow-up sequence with 3 emails at 5, 10, and 21 days. Guest Prep Kit: Pre-interview questionnaire, 3 key messages, 2-3 stories to tell, technical setup checklist, promotion plan, and what to ask the host.

**Expected output:** Complete podcast outreach system with pitch templates and guest preparation kit
**Pro tip:** Offer to promote the episode to your audience — hosts care more about distribution than content

### 1.25 UTM and Tracking Link Builder
**Use case:** Create a systematic approach to tracking marketing links with consistent parameters
**Best for:** Any marketer running multi-channel campaigns

You are a marketing analytics specialist. I need a complete UTM parameter system so I can track which marketing efforts actually drive results.

My business: [name] | Website: [URL] | Channels I use: [list your marketing channels] | Campaigns running: [current or planned] | Analytics platform: [Google Analytics 4, Plausible, Mixpanel, etc.]

Design a UTM parameter system. Naming Convention: Standardized structure for each parameter including utm_source values for each channel (consistent names), utm_medium values for each type, utm_campaign structure following [campaign name]-[year]-[month], utm_content for differentiating similar links, and utm_term for paid keywords. Channel-Specific Guidelines: Specific parameter values to use for each channel, what not to include, and common mistakes to avoid. Link Management: Tool recommendations, link shortening strategy, spreadsheet template to track all links, and monthly audit process. Quality Control Checklist: Pre-campaign QA process including testing all links, verifying in preview, checking for typos, ensuring lowercase consistency, and confirming naming convention compliance.

**Expected output:** Complete UTM naming convention document with channel guidelines and QC checklist
**Pro tip:** Create a shared Google Sheet or use Google Campaign URL Builder to ensure your team uses consistent parameters

### 1.26 Abandoned Cart Email Sequence
**Use case:** Recover lost sales with automated abandoned cart emails
**Best for:** E-commerce businesses, SaaS companies with free trials

Act as an email marketing specialist focused on conversion rate optimization. I need a high-converting abandoned cart or abandoned trial recovery sequence.

My product: [product or service] | Average cart or trial value: [value] | Abandonment rate: [percentage if known] | Primary reason for abandonment: [price, distractions, comparison shopping] | Customer persona: [brief description]

Create a 5-email recovery sequence. Email 1 — Friendly Reminder (1 hour after abandonment): Gentle nudge assuming good intent. Include product image and clear recovery button. Subject line is personal and low-pressure. Email 2 — Social Proof (24 hours): Show others like them made the same choice. Include specific testimonial, rating highlight, usage statistic, and case study snippet with a number. Email 3 — Value Reinforcement (48 hours): Address the top hesitation reason. If price show ROI calculation or payment option. If trust show guarantees or media features. If commitment show onboarding simplicity. Email 4 — Incentive Offer (72 hours): Time-limited incentive such as discount code, free shipping, bonus resource, or extended trial. State value clearly with expiration. Email 5 — Final Notice (5-7 days): Summary of value proposition and what they are missing. Leave the door open with a lower-commitment option.

For each email provide: subject line (3 options), preview text, body copy, button text and color, and optimal send time.

**Expected output:** Complete 5-email abandoned recovery sequence with full copy for each email
**Pro tip:** Email 1 at 1 hour and Email 4 at 72 hours with the incentive consistently drive the most recoveries

### 1.27 Referral Program Design
**Use case:** Create a referral program that turns customers into a growth channel
**Best for:** Any business with happy customers

Act as a viral marketing strategist who has designed referral programs for B2B and B2C companies. I need a complete referral program design.

My product: [product or service] | My customers: [who buys from you] | Customer satisfaction: [NPS score, retention rate, or qualitative] | Average LTV: [lifetime value] | Current customer count: [number] | What makes my product referable: [inherent shareability]

Design a referral program covering these areas. Incentive Structure: Evaluate double-sided rewards, single-sided, charitable donation, gamified tiers, and access-based models. Recommend the best with exact reward value, why it works relative to LTV, payout timing, and delivery mechanism. Program Rules: Eligibility criteria, tracking method (cookie, link, code), reward cap, fraud prevention, terms and conditions essentials, and expiration policy. Customer Experience: The referral flow from customer discovery through sharing, landing page experience, conversion tracking, and reward delivery with optimization tips for each step. Promotion Strategy: Triggered emails at milestones, in-app placement, post-purchase page, social campaigns, email signature, and personal check-in calls for high-value customers. Measurement: Key metrics including referral rate, referred customer conversion rate, referred LTV versus organic LTV, viral coefficient, and program ROI.

**Expected output:** Complete referral program design with incentive structure, rules, and launch plan
**Pro tip:** The best referral programs make customers feel like insiders sharing a secret — status often outperforms cash rewards

### 1.28 Community Building Blueprint
**Use case:** Launch and grow an engaged community around your brand
**Best for:** Brand builders, community managers, founders

Act as a community building expert who has grown online communities from zero to thousands of engaged members. I need a complete community launch plan.

My brand: [name] | My audience: [who the community would serve] | Community purpose: [support, networking, education, feedback, brand advocacy] | Platform choice: [Slack, Discord, Circle, Facebook Group, or need recommendation] | Current audience size: [potential members to invite] | Available time for management: [hours per week]

Create a blueprint with these sections. Community Foundation: Purpose and values statement, member promise, norms and guidelines, and decision on public versus private and free versus paid. Launch Strategy: Pre-launch phase including teasing the community, collecting early interest, and identifying 5-10 founding members. Soft launch invite-only with first 50 members. Public launch with onboarding flow and welcome sequence. Content and Engagement Loops: Daily engagement drivers like question of the day. Weekly rhythm with predictable content cadence. Monthly events like themed challenges, virtual meetups, and feedback circles. Moderation System: Moderator roles, conflict resolution framework, escalation path, automated tools, and community health metrics. Monetization Paths: If applicable, premium membership tier, sponsored content, job board, marketplace, or events.

**Expected output:** Complete community building blueprint from foundation through launch to growth
**Pro tip:** The first 100 members determine your community culture — choose them carefully and engage deeply

### 1.29 Visual Content Brief Creator
**Use case:** Write detailed creative briefs for designers, videographers, and visual creators
**Best for:** Marketing teams working with visual creators

Act as a creative director who bridges marketing strategy and visual execution. I need to write a detailed creative brief for visual content.

Campaign or asset type: [social graphic, video ad, infographic, photo shoot, illustration] | Brand: [name and existing guidelines] | Goal: [what this content must achieve] | Audience: [who will see it] | Platform and dimensions: [where it will appear] | Key message: [the single thing viewers must understand] | Tone: [professional, playful, urgent, warm]

Write a complete brief with these sections. Project Overview: Asset description, delivery specs, deadline, budget range, and success criteria. Background and Context: Why this project exists, what problem it solves, and relevant past assets. Audience Insight: Who we are talking to, what they currently think, and what we want them to think after seeing this. Creative Direction: Mood references, what TO do, what NOT to do, brand elements required, typography, and color palette. Messaging Hierarchy: Primary message as the largest prominent element, secondary supporting copy, tertiary details, and visual hierarchy notes. Do's and Don'ts: 3-5 specific do's and don'ts with examples. Technical Specifications: Dimensions, formats, resolution minimums, file size limits, text-safe areas, platform requirements, and accessibility needs.

**Expected output:** Complete visual creative brief ready to hand to a designer or creative team
**Pro tip:** Include visual examples of what NOT to do — showing what you want to avoid is often more helpful than describing what you want

### 1.30 Partner Co-Marketing Proposal Template
**Use case:** Create partnership proposals for joint marketing with complementary brands
**Best for:** Growth marketers, partnership managers

Act as a business development strategist focused on strategic partnerships. I need a partnership proposal template to approach complementary brands.

My brand: [name and description] | My audience: [size and description] | What I can offer a partner: [audience access, content creation, email promotion, social sharing, product bundling, event collaboration] | Ideal partner profile: [type of business, audience overlap] | Goal of partnership: [audience growth, revenue sharing, authority building]

Create a partnership proposal covering these sections. Partnership Concept Overview: One-page summary with partnership name, both brands involved, shared audience benefit, partnership format, expected outcome for each brand, and timeline. Value Exchange Matrix: Table showing what each party contributes and receives including audience reach, specific assets, and promotion effort. Audience Overlap Analysis: How the audiences complement each other, alignment points, combined potential reach, and why this benefits both audiences. Campaign Mechanics: Step-by-step process including launch date, content creation responsibilities, promotion schedule, tracking method, and communication cadence. Measurement and ROI: Success metrics for each brand, tracking implementation, reporting schedule, and definition of success. Partnership Agreement Terms: Duration, exclusivity, cancellation terms, intellectual property ownership, and revenue sharing.

**Expected output:** Complete partnership proposal template with all sections ready to customize
**Pro tip:** When approaching a partner, lead with what you can GIVE them, not what you want in return

### 1.31 Ad Creative Fatigue Detection and Refresh System
**Use case:** Identify when ads stop performing and know exactly what to refresh
**Best for:** Paid media managers, business owners running ads

Apply reverse engineering to build an ad fatigue detection and refresh system. Start with the goal: maintain consistent ad performance by detecting fatigue early and knowing which creative element to refresh.

My ad platform: [Facebook, Google, LinkedIn, TikTok] | Creative types: [image, video, carousel, text] | Current performance: [CTR, CPC, CPA, frequency] | My industry: [industry] | Average campaign duration: [how long campaigns typically run]

Build the system. Fatigue Detection Framework: Early warning signs including frequency thresholds when ads typically fatigue, performance metric shifts indicating fatigue versus normal fluctuation, engagement pattern changes, and time-based signals. Diagnostic Assessment: Is it the creative, the copy, the offer, or the audience? If CTR dropped but CPA stable: visual fatigue. If CTR stable but CPA increased: audience saturation. If both dropped: message fatigue. Refresh Strategy by Element: When refreshing copy, change the hook pattern, CTA type, or offer framing while keeping the successful visual. When refreshing visuals, change color palette, image style, or focal point while keeping successful copy. When refreshing audiences, expand lookalike, layer new interests, or test new placements. Refresh Cadence Calendar: Day 0 launch, Day 7 first copy refresh, Day 14 visual refresh, Day 21 angle refresh, Day 28 full overhaul or archive.

**Expected output:** Complete ad fatigue detection and refresh system with specific thresholds and actions
**Pro tip:** Change ONE variable at a time when refreshing ads — changing everything at once means you will not know what worked

### 1.32 Webinar Promotion Campaign
**Use case:** Plan and execute a full promotional campaign for an upcoming webinar
**Best for:** Marketers running educational or sales webinars

Act as a demand generation specialist who fills webinars consistently. I need a complete 14-day promotional campaign for my webinar.

Webinar details: topic, date and time, speaker or host, target audience, registration page URL, format (live, automated, hybrid), and goal (attendance target, leads, sales).

Build the campaign across these periods. Pre-Webinar (Weeks -2 to -1): Early bird promotion for warmest leads, speaker network leverage, social media teasers with countdown and pain point content, 3-email invitation sequence to your list over 7 days, and partner cross-promotion with 3 complementary partners. Week Before Webinar: Registration confirmation email, calendar invite, social media engagement push with questions and polls, last-chance emails (2-3), and LinkedIn or Facebook event setup. Day of Webinar: Morning-of reminder, 30-minutes-before reminder with direct join link, social media posts, and community reminders. During Webinar: Live engagement prompts like polls and Q and A, offer and CTA delivery timing, and technical backup plan. Post-Webinar (Week +1): Thank-you email with recording link within 2 hours, survey request, content repurposing plan, non-attendee outreach, attendee nurture sequence with 3 emails, and sales follow-up for qualified leads.

**Expected output:** Complete 14-day webinar promotion plan with email sequences and content calendar
**Pro tip:** The single biggest lever for webinar attendance is the number of reminder emails — send at least 4

### 1.33 Brand Story Framework
**Use case:** Develop and articulate your brand's origin story in a compelling way
**Best for:** Founders, brand marketers, PR

Act as a brand narrative consultant who helps companies articulate their founding stories in compelling ways. Guide me through the Brand Story Arc framework.

My company: [name] | Founder(s): [names and backgrounds] | Year founded: [year] | Original problem: [the initial insight or frustration] | Key milestone: [a pivotal moment] | Our mission: [what drives us] | Our audience: [who we serve]

Guide through 8 sections. Act 1 — The Origin: The World Before (what was the status quo), The Inciting Incident (the specific moment that sparked the idea), The Decision (the moment the founders committed and what was at stake). Act 2 — The Journey: The Struggle (honest challenges and what almost broke the company), The Breakthrough (the turning point), The Growth (key milestones as proof of commitment). Act 3 — The Purpose: The Mission Today (bigger picture beyond profit), The Invitation (how the customer fits into this story). For each section provide what to include, what tone to strike, what to avoid, and a fill-in-the-blank template.

**Expected output:** Complete brand story document following the 8-section story arc framework
**Pro tip:** The most powerful brand stories come from vulnerability — share a real failure or struggle, not just successes

### 1.34 Landing Page Copy Architecture
**Use case:** Structure a high-converting landing page with strategic copy layout
**Best for:** Marketers, founders building conversion pages

Act as a conversion copywriter who has built landing pages that convert at 15%+ consistently. I need a complete landing page structure and copy.

Product or offer: [what you are selling] | Target audience: [who the page is for] | Primary goal: [signup, purchase, demo request, download] | Key objections: [top 3 reasons people do not convert] | Traffic source: [where visitors come from]

Create the architecture. Above the Fold (Hero Section): 5 headline options using outcome-driven, question-based, curiosity-gap, bold promise, or for-audience formulas. Subheadline that expands with specificity. Primary CTA button text in 5 options. Supporting elements like social proof bar and trust signals. Middle Section Flow: Organize in optimal order: Pain Point Amplifier, Solution Introduction, How It Works in 3-4 steps, Features and Benefits as benefits first, Social Proof with 3 testimonials and logos, Objection Handlers as FAQ addressing top 5 objections, Risk Reversal with guarantee, and Scarcity or Urgency if authentic. Conversion Section: Final CTA with headline, subheadline, primary and secondary button, and final risk reversal. Below the Fold: Footer elements, trust badges, legal disclaimers, and exit-intent popup if applicable. Mobile Optimization Notes.

**Expected output:** Complete landing page architecture with copy for each section and mobile guidance
**Pro tip:** Above-the-fold is not just the hero section — test different fold positions; sometimes a shorter page converts better

### 1.35 Podcast Show Notes and SEO Optimizer
**Use case:** Write podcast show notes that rank in search and drive listens
**Best for:** Podcasters, content marketers

Act as a podcast SEO specialist who helps shows grow through search discovery. I need optimized show notes for an episode.

Podcast name: [your podcast] | Episode title: [title] | Guest name: [if applicable] | Episode summary: [2-3 sentences] | Key topics: [list] | Key takeaways: [main points] | Guest bio: [one paragraph] | Links mentioned: [resources, URLs]

Write complete show notes. SEO-Optimized Title: [Episode Topic]: [Guest Name] on [Compelling Hook] — [Podcast Name]. Plus 3 backup options. Meta Description (under 160 characters): Summarize with keywords, hook, and guest mention. Episode Overview (2-3 paragraphs): What the episode covers, why it matters now, who should listen. Timestamped Highlights: 5-7 timestamps with compelling descriptions. Key Quotes: 3-5 quotable moments with click-to-tweet. Resources and Links: Organized into Books, Tools, People, Previous Episodes, Guest Links. About the Guest: 2-3 paragraph bio. Social Media Promotion Suite: LinkedIn post (3 options), Twitter thread (10 tweets), Instagram story slides (5 concepts), newsletter blurb (100 words).

**Expected output:** Complete show notes package with SEO metadata, timestamps, quotes, and social promotion
**Pro tip:** Publish show notes at the same time as the episode — Google prioritizes same-day published content

### 1.36 Hashtag Research and Strategy
**Use case:** Build a data-driven hashtag system for social media growth
**Best for:** Social media managers, content creators

Act as a social media growth strategist who uses hashtags as a discovery engine. I need a complete hashtag strategy.

My account or brand: [name] | My niche: [industry or topic] | Platform: [Instagram, TikTok, LinkedIn, Twitter, YouTube] | Target audience: [who should find my content] | Content themes: [what you typically post about]

Build a hashtag system. Research Methodology: How to find the best hashtags using search algorithm patterns, competitor analysis, content-type specific tags, and trending tag monitoring. Tag Tier System: Tier 1 Broad (1M+ posts) use 1-2 for reach, Tier 2 Medium (100K-1M) use 3-5, Tier 3 Niche (10K-100K) use 5-7, Tier 4 Hyper-Niche (under 10K) use 3-5, Tier 5 Branded use 1-2. Tag Sets by Content Type: 5 different sets for educational, entertainment, promotional, behind-the-scenes, and trending content. Posting Strategy: Where to place hashtags, rotation frequency, banned tags to avoid, and A/B testing approach. Performance Tracking: Weekly review tracking which tags drove impressions, engagement, and profile visits.

**Expected output:** Complete hashtag system with tiered tags, content-specific sets, and tracking process
**Pro tip:** Do not use the same 30 hashtags on every post — rotate between 3-4 different sets

### 1.37 Direct Mail Postcard Script
**Use case:** Write a high-converting direct mail postcard or letter
**Best for:** Local businesses, B2B sales teams, real estate

Act as a direct mail copywriter who has generated millions in response through postal campaigns. I need a complete direct mail piece.

My offer: [what you are selling or promoting] | Target recipient: [who receives this] | My business: [name and description] | Response mechanism: [call, visit website, bring coupon, scan QR code] | Goal: [appointment, sale, lead, event attendance]

Write the piece. Envelope Teaser: What goes on the outside to ensure opening. Options include handwritten-style address, curiosity statement, benefit teaser, or official-looking format. Body Copy: Paragraph 1 personalizes showing you know their situation. Paragraph 2 agitates the problem. Paragraph 3 presents your solution. Paragraph 4 provides social proof. Paragraph 5 gives offer details and guarantees. Paragraph 6 is the call to action. Paragraph 7 is the PS which is the most-read element after the headline. Response Mechanism: Phone number, URL, QR code with instructions, reply card, or store visit instructions.

**Expected output:** Complete direct mail piece with envelope strategy, headline options, and full body copy
**Pro tip:** The PS is the second-most-read element after the headline — always include one with your main offer restated

### 1.38 YouTube Thumbnail and Title Optimization
**Use case:** Increase click-through rate on YouTube videos through better titles and thumbnails
**Best for:** YouTubers, video content creators

Act as a YouTube growth specialist who understands the algorithm and viewer psychology. I need to optimize a video CTR.

Video topic: [what the video is about] | Target audience: [who should click] | Video format: [tutorial, vlog, review, commentary, educational, entertainment] | What makes this video unique: [specific angle] | Competing videos: [example titles and thumbnails]

Generate title and thumbnail optimizations. Title Optimization: 5 title options using How To, List or Number, Question challenging common belief, Bold Statement, and For Audience formulas. For each provide character count, keyword optimization, clickability score (1-10), and rationale. Thumbnail Design: 4 concepts — Before and After, Face Plus Expression, Text Overlay, and Comparison. For each specify image composition, facial expression, text content and placement, color palette, font choice, and visual hierarchy. A/B Testing Plan: Test different thumbnails over first 24 hours, compare CTR after 1K impressions.

**Expected output:** Complete title and thumbnail optimization with 5 title options and 4 thumbnail concepts
**Pro tip:** The title and thumbnail should tell a story together — one should not make sense without the other

### 1.39 Email List Growth Campaign
**Use case:** Design a multi-pronged campaign to grow your email subscriber list

Act as an email list building strategist. I need a campaign to grow my email subscribers.

My website: [URL] | My niche: [industry or topic] | Current list size: [number] | Lead magnet: [what people get upon signup, or need one created] | Target new subscribers per month: [goal] | Traffic sources: [blog, social media, YouTube, podcast]

Design a 4-week growth campaign. Lead Magnet Optimization: If you have one, audit for headline, format, delivery, and perceived value. If you need one, recommend 3 concepts (checklist, template, guide, toolkit, mini-course, calculator, swipe file) that would convert. Traffic Source Strategies: For each source specify signup form placement, content upgrade strategy, CTA optimization, and timing. Signup Page Optimization: Structure with headline, subheadline, bullet benefits, minimal form fields, CTA button text options, and trust signals. Incentive Layering: Immediate value upon signup, 24-hour follow-up, 72-hour engagement check. Promotion Calendar: Week 1 launch to existing audience and social media. Week 2 guest content on 3 platforms plus one partnership. Week 3 content upgrade for top content plus social round 2. Week 4 referral incentive plus partnership round 2.

**Expected output:** Complete 4-week list growth campaign with lead magnet strategy and promotion calendar
**Pro tip:** A single high-converting lead magnet at 15%+ conversion rate beats 5 mediocre ones

### 1.40 Crisis Communication Statement
**Use case:** Draft a carefully worded response to a business crisis or PR issue
**Best for:** Founders, PR teams, business leaders

Act as a crisis communication specialist who has handled PR crises for startups and established companies. I need a carefully crafted statement.

The situation: [describe the issue without revealing unnecessary sensitive details] | My company: [name] | Stakeholders affected: [customers, employees, investors, partners, public] | Confirmed facts: [what is confirmed true right now] | Actions taken so far: [what you have done] | Desired outcome: [what you want the result to be] | Tone preference: [empathetic, factual, apologetic, confident, or combination]

Draft a statement following this framework. Step 1 — Acknowledge and Validate: First paragraph acknowledges the situation without being defensive. Validates concerns. Step 2 — Take Responsibility Where Appropriate: Clear statement of responsibility. No blame-shifting. Step 3 — Define the Facts: What is confirmed, what is under investigation, what is not true. Step 4 — Action Plan: Immediate actions, short-term fixes, long-term changes, timeline. Step 5 — Commitment: Restatement of company values. Also provide an internal version for employees and a social media version condensed for 2-3 posts.

**Expected output:** Complete crisis communication statement with internal and external versions
**Pro tip:** Speed of response is critical — a statement within 2 hours is ideal, but accuracy matters more

### 1.41 Marketing Automation Flow Map
**Use case:** Design automated marketing sequences triggered by user behavior
**Best for:** Marketers using automation platforms

Act as a marketing automation consultant who builds complex flows that nurture leads on autopilot. I need an automation flow designed.

My business: [type] | My platform: [marketing automation tool] | My audience: [who you market to] | Key triggers: [website visit, email open, purchase, link click, form submission]

Design a complete automation ecosystem. Welcome or Acquisition Flow: Triggered by new subscriber via specific source. Tag by source. Send welcome sequence (3-5 emails). Score lead based on engagement. Move to appropriate nurture flow. Lead Scoring System: Positive actions (+points for email open, link click, page visit, demo request) and negative actions (-points for unsubscribe, spam complaint, inactivity). Score thresholds: cold (under 20), warm (20-50), hot (50+). Behavior-Based Flows: Abandoned cart flow (5 emails over 7 days), content consumer flow (triggered by 3+ blog reads), product interest flow (triggered by pricing page visit), re-engagement flow (triggered by 90 days no opens). Purchase or Conversion Flows: Post-purchase confirmation, onboarding, value delivery, upsell. Trial start flow: Day 1 setup, Day 3 best practices, Day 5 case studies, Day 7 success stories, Day 10 conversion offer. Conditional Logic: Map decision points for each flow. Health Monitoring: Monthly audit of engagement rates per flow, drop-off points, conversions per flow, unsubscribes by segment.

**Expected output:** Complete automation ecosystem map with triggers, actions, and scoring
**Pro tip:** The most common automation mistake is over-automating — keep a human touch trigger in every flow

### 1.42 Voice of Customer (VoC) Analysis
**Use case:** Analyze customer feedback, reviews, or support tickets for patterns
**Best for:** Product teams, customer experience managers

Act as a customer insights analyst who extracts actionable patterns from qualitative feedback. I need to analyze customer voices.

Source data type: [reviews, support tickets, survey responses, social media comments, sales call transcripts] | Customer segment: [who these customers are] | Volume of feedback: [approximate number of data points] | Specific question: [what insight you are looking for]

Apply this VOICE analysis framework. Step 1 — Sentiment Analysis: Overall sentiment distribution (positive, negative, neutral). Intensity scoring. Sentiment trends over time. Step 2 — Theme Extraction: Identify recurring themes grouped into Product features, Pricing, Support, UX, Competitor comparisons, and Unmet needs. For each provide frequency count, representative quotes, sentiment breakdown, and verbatim examples. Step 3 — Pain Point Prioritization: Rank by frequency, severity, business impact, and ease of fix. Create a priority matrix with Quick Wins, Strategic Improvements, Low Priority, and Monitor. Step 4 — Opportunity Identification: Unmet needs representing product opportunities. Requests for nonexistent features. Pains competitors could solve. Jobs to be done. Step 5 — Actionable Recommendations: Top 5 actions based on analysis with what to do, why it matters, estimated effort, and success metric.

**Expected output:** Complete VoC analysis with themes, pain points, opportunities, and recommendations
**Pro tip:** Look for the gap between what customers praise and what they complain about — that is often where the biggest opportunity lives

### 1.43 Seasonal Marketing Calendar
**Use case:** Plan marketing activities around key seasonal moments
**Best for:** Content marketers, social media managers, e-commerce

Act as a seasonal marketing strategist who helps businesses capitalize on timely moments. I need a seasonal marketing calendar.

My business: [describe] | My industry: [industry] | Target audience: [who you sell to] | Products or services: [what you offer] | Key seasons or holidays: [list if known] | Marketing channels: [where you promote]

Create a 12-month seasonal marketing calendar. Monthly Overview: For each month list relevant holidays and observances, industry-specific moments (conferences, trade shows, awareness months), cultural moments, and seasonal audience mindset shifts (budgeting season, planning season, spending season). Content Opportunities: For each seasonal moment provide content angle, ideal format, promotional strategy, and connection to your product. Deadline Calendar: Content creation deadlines, promotion start dates, peak engagement windows, and post-event follow-up timing. Budget Allocation Guide: Recommended ad spend distribution across months, content production timing, and resource allocation. Quick-Win Opportunities: For the next 30 days, specific content ideas, promotion tactics, and engagement strategies.

**Expected output:** Complete 12-month seasonal marketing calendar with deadlines and content opportunities
**Pro tip:** Do not try to capitalize on every holiday — pick 5-8 most relevant to your audience and go deep

### 1.44 Facebook Group Growth Strategy

Create a growth strategy. Group Foundation: Name (keyword-optimized), description (above and below fold), cover image guidance, membership questions (3 screening questions), and posting rules. Content Strategy: 5 weekly content pillars rotating daily — Monday question or discussion, Tuesday educational tip, Wednesday member spotlight, Thursday resource share, Friday fun, Weekend community building. Growth Tactics (Organic): Cross-promotion with complementary groups, guest expert takeovers (1-2 per month), member referral incentives, content sharing to related groups, and collaboration with members.
