### 1.45 Customer Win-Back Sequence
**Use case:** Re-engage lapsed customers who have not purchased in a while
**Best for:** E-commerce, SaaS, subscription businesses

Act as a customer retention specialist who wins back lost customers systematically. I need a win-back campaign.

My business: [type] | Average customer lifespan: [how long typically active] | Churn triggers: [what typically causes leaving] | What we offer: [product or service] | Inactive definition: [no purchase for X months, no login for X days] | Offer for returning: [discount, new feature, free month, or need recommendation]

Design a multi-touch win-back campaign. Segmentation: Recent inactives (30-60 days), Mid-term inactives (60-180 days), Long-term inactives (180+ days), High-value inactives (based on past LTV). Win-Back Sequence: Touch 1 — The We Miss You (gentle, focus on what they are missing, highlight what has changed). Touch 2 — The What Is New (showcase improvements since they left, before versus now format). Touch 3 — The Come Back Offer (specific incentive with clear expiration). Touch 4 — The Last Chance (gentle final push, leave door open, feedback option). Touch 5 — The We Value You (3-question survey asking why they left). Channel Mix: Email for all segments, SMS for mobile users, social retargeting, and direct outreach for high-value only.

**Expected output:** Complete win-back sequence with segmentation, messaging, and offers for each tier
**Pro tip:** The most effective win-back tactic is showing customers what has improved since they left

### 1.46 Influencer Content Brief Template
**Use case:** Give clear creative direction to influencers you have hired
**Best for:** Brand managers, influencer marketing coordinators

Act as an influencer marketing manager who ensures brand-consistent content from creator partners. Write a creative brief for an influencer.

Campaign name: [name] | Brand: [name] | Product featured: [product] | Influencer name: [name] | Campaign dates: [start to end] | Platform(s): [Instagram, TikTok, YouTube] | Campaign goal: [awareness, conversions, engagement, brand affinity] | Key message: [the single most important thing]

Write a complete brief. Campaign Overview: Brand background (2-3 sentences), product description, campaign theme, and target audience. Creative Direction: Preferred content format, visual direction with mood and aesthetic references, and audio suggestions. Messaging Guidelines: Key message, supporting points, brand language to use, and brand language to avoid including competitor names and over-promising. Disclosures and Legal: Required disclosure format, FTC compliance, approved claims, and prohibited claims. Deliverables Checklist: Number of posts, formats, aspect ratios, caption length, hashtags, tagging requirements, due dates, and approval process. Content Examples: 2-3 example concepts with caption structures and visual descriptions. Technical Specs: File format, resolution, aspect ratios, text-safe areas, and delivery method.

**Expected output:** Complete influencer content brief covering all creative and legal requirements
**Pro tip:** Give influencers creative freedom within guardrails — the best branded content does not feel like an ad

### 1.47 Google Business Profile Optimizer
**Use case:** Fully optimize a Google Business Profile for local SEO
**Best for:** Local businesses, brick-and-mortar stores, service-area businesses

Act as a local SEO specialist who helps businesses dominate Google Maps and local search. I need to fully optimize my Google Business Profile.

Business name: [name] | Category: [primary category] | Address or service area: [location] | Phone: [phone] | Website: [URL] | Business hours: [hours] | Products or services: [what you offer]

Create a complete optimization plan. Basic Info: Business name (keyword inclusion within guidelines), category selection (primary plus secondary recommendations), service area or address decision, attributes to select, and 500+ character description with keywords and value proposition. Visual Content: Photos needed (exterior, interior, product shots, team, service in action, before and after) with composition guidance. Video: 30-60 second walkthrough, testimonial video, product demo. Review Generation: How to ask for reviews at post-service, via text, email, in-person, QR code. Response templates for positive, neutral, and negative reviews. Posts Strategy: Weekly post types (offer, event, product, update). Posting frequency. Q and A Management: Monitor incoming questions, pre-populate FAQ with 10-15 Q and As. Insights and Optimization: Monthly review of search queries, views sources, customer actions, and competitor comparison.

**Expected output:** Complete Google Business Profile optimization plan with content and management systems
**Pro tip:** Your GBP description is NOT your website about page — write for someone with LOCAL intent

### 1.48 Marketing Budget Allocation Model
**Use case:** Create a framework for deciding how to allocate a limited marketing budget
**Best for:** Founders, marketing managers with budget responsibility

Act as a fractional marketing CFO who helps businesses allocate limited budgets for maximum ROI. I need a budget allocation model.

My business: [describe] | Total monthly marketing budget: [amount] | Target customers: [who I sell to] | Primary channel currently: [what is working] | Revenue goal from marketing: [target] | Average LTV: [lifetime value] | Current CAC: [if known] | Gross margin: [percentage]

Build a budget allocation model. Channel Economics: For each potential channel estimate expected CAC, acquisition volume per month, time to breakeven, scalability ceiling, and confidence level. Channels to evaluate include SEO, Google Ads, Facebook Ads, LinkedIn Ads, Content Marketing, Email, Influencer, Events, Partnerships, Direct Mail. Portfolio Allocation: Proven Performers (40-60%), Scale Tests (20-30%), New Experiments (10-20%), Flex or Overflow (10%). ROI Projection Model: For recommended allocation project total acquisitions, blended CAC, revenue, cost, net ROI, and payback period. Phased Ramp Plan: Month 1 heavy investment in proven channels plus one test. Month 2 scale winners, add another test. Month 3 rebalance based on data. Success Metrics: North Star for budget efficiency, leading indicators, lagging indicators, and reporting cadence.

**Expected output:** Complete budget allocation model with channel economics and ROI projections
**Pro tip:** The most dangerous marketing budget trap is spray and pray — concentrate spend on 1-2 proven channels

### 1.49 Product Launch Waitlist Strategy
**Use case:** Build anticipation and capture leads before a product launches
**Best for:** Pre-launch products, course creators, SaaS founders

Act as a launch strategist specializing in pre-launch audience building. I need a waitlist and early-access strategy.

Product: [what you are launching] | Launch date: [when it goes live] | Target customer: [who will buy] | Unique value proposition: [what makes it special] | Pre-launch audience: [current email list, followers, or zero] | Price point: [expected price] | Waitlist incentive: [discount, early access, bonus, or need suggestion]

Design a complete waitlist campaign. Waitlist Landing Page: Headline (outcome-focused), subheadline (early access promise), social proof from beta testers, list of what they get, incentive for joining early, minimal form fields, and share mechanism after signup. Incentive Structure: Tiered by signup position. First 100 get biggest bonus. 101-500 get moderate bonus. 500+ get base incentive. Referral tier: refer 3 friends for additional bonus. Pre-Launch Content Sequence: Week 1 behind the scenes and founder story. Week 2 sne peek and feature preview. Week 3 social proof with beta results. Week 4 education on how to maximize value. Week 5+ urgency build with countdown. Referral Loop: Built-in sharing mechanism after signup, leaderboard for top referrers, bonus rewards at referral milestones. Launch Day: Announcement to waitlist, tiered access, real-time social proof. Post-Launch: Conversion tracking, non-converting follow-up, unconverted follow-up with alternative offer.

**Expected output:** Complete waitlist strategy with landing page, content sequence, and referral mechanics
**Pro tip:** The most effective waitlist incentive is early access to a limited supply — scarcity beats discounts

### 1.50 YouTube Video Descriptions and Chapters
**Use case:** Write optimized YouTube descriptions with timestamps and chapters
**Best for:** YouTubers, video content creators

Act as a YouTube SEO specialist. I need an optimized video description with timestamps, chapters, and metadata.

Video title: [your title] | Video topic: [what it is about] | Target keyword: [primary search term] | Video length: [duration] | Key sections: [list of topics in order] | Your channel: [name and topic] | Links to mention: [website, social, related videos, resources]

Write a complete description. First 2-3 Lines (Above the Fold): What YouTube shows before Show More. Must include primary keyword naturally. Must hook the viewer. Structure: value statement plus what they will learn plus keyword. Timestamped Chapters: [00:00] Intro with hook description, [01:23] Chapter 1 topic, [05:45] Chapter 2, [10:12] Chapter 3, [15:30] Chapter 4, [18:45] Key Takeaway, [20:00] CTA. Each chapter includes 1-2 keywords. Resources Section: Organized with Related Videos, Mentioned Resources, Tools Used, Free Guide, Gear or Equipment. About Section: 2-3 sentences about your channel, who it is for. Social and Connect: Other platforms, newsletter, website. Hashtags: 3-5 at bottom mixing broad and niche.

**Expected output:** Complete YouTube description with chapters, links, and metadata
**Pro tip:** YouTube uses watch time AND description keywords to understand your content — make chapter descriptions detailed

### 1.51 Content Repurposing Checklist for Marketing
**Use case:** Systematically repurpose marketing content across all channels
**Best for:** Content marketers, social media managers

Act as a content operations specialist. I need a systematic repurposing checklist that ensures every piece of marketing content reaches maximum audience.

Original asset: [blog post, video, podcast, infographic, report] | Topic: [topic] | Key data or quotes: [notable elements to extract] | Target platforms: [all platforms] | Team capacity: [hours available for repurposing]

Create a repurposing checklist. Immediate Repurposing (Same Day): Extract 3-5 quotable lines for social media. Create 3 social media posts with different angles. Write email teaser to list. Submit to 2-3 relevant Slack or Discord communities. 24-Hour Repurposing: Create visual quote card from best line. Record 60-second video summarizing key point. Write LinkedIn long-form post. Create Twitter thread of 10-15 tweets. 48-72 Hour Repurposing: Turn into step-by-step tutorial if applicable. Create checklist or cheatsheet version. Submit to 1-2 industry roundups or newsletters. Record podcast micro-episode (5-10 min). Week 2 Repurposing: Create slide deck version for SlideShare. Turn into guest post pitch for industry blogs. Create infographic or visual summary. Develop mini email course (3-5 emails) from the content. Month 2 Repurposing: Update and refresh for new data. Combine with related content to create ebook or guide. Repurpose for different audience segment with adjusted messaging.

**Expected output:** Complete repurposing checklist with timeline and platform-specific adaptation notes
**Pro tip:** Create once, repurpose seven times — the first repurpose (immediate social posts) drives 60% of the total value

**Expected output:** Marketing ROI dashboard template with KPI definitions, data source integration guide, and review meeting agenda

### 1.67 A/B Testing Methodology and Experimentation Framework
**Use case:** Design and execute statistically valid A/B tests that produce actionable results
**Best for:** Growth marketers, conversion rate optimization specialists

Act as a CRO and experimentation specialist. Design a rigorous A/B testing framework for [brand] testing [page/element type] with current traffic of [monthly visitors]. Cover the full testing lifecycle: hypothesis generation (using the ICE framework: Impact, Confidence, Ease scoring), test design (control vs. [number] variants, randomization method, minimum sample size calculation using [desired lift] [statistical power] [significance level]), duration planning (how long to run based on traffic volume, day-of-week effects, seasonality considerations), execution (tool selection recommendations, QA checklist for test setup, segment targeting), analysis (statistical significance calculation, practical significance vs. statistical significance, secondary metric impact analysis, novelty effect detection), and decision framework (how to decide between launch, iterate, kill, or retest). Include a test prioritization backlog template and an experimentation calendar that ensures tests don't cannibalize each other.

**Expected output:** End-to-end testing playbook with sample size calculator, test plan template, and decision matrix
**Pro tip:** Run every test for at least two full business cycles (14 days minimum) because one-week tests miss weekend behavior patterns that often reverse results.

### 1.68 A/B Testing Results Documentation and Knowledge Base
**Use case:** Document test results systematically so insights accumulate rather than disappear
**Best for:** Experimentation teams, marketing operations

Act as a testing operations manager. Create a standardized A/B test documentation template for a team running [number] tests per month across [channels/touchpoints]. The template must capture: test ID and name, hypothesis statement, start and end dates, sample sizes per variant, primary and secondary metrics with absolute and relative lifts, statistical significance (p-value, confidence intervals), segment breakdowns (new vs. returning, device type, traffic source, customer segment), screenshots of each variant, unexpected observations, and final decision + rationale. Provide a knowledge base structure (tag taxonomy, search conventions, quarterly insight synthesis format) and a governance process for when expired tests auto-archive. Include a weekly experimentation retrospective template that aggregates top learnings for leadership.

**Expected output:** Test documentation template, knowledge base architecture, and retro meeting agenda with aggregation format
**Pro tip:** The real value of A/B testing compounds over time, not from single wins, so a searchable test library is worth more than any individual test result.

**Best for:** Multi-location brand marketers, franchise marketing managers

Act as a multi-location SEO and reputation management strategist. Build a scalable local marketing system for [brand] with [number] locations across [region]. Include centralized vs. localized content strategy (which pages are templated (hours, services, about) vs. locally unique (community involvement, local reviews responses, location-specific offers), location page optimization framework (unique content requirements per location, photo standards, schema markup with location-specific structured data), review management at scale (automated review monitoring across all locations, AI-assisted response drafting with local personalization, escalation protocol for crisis reviews, review sentiment trend reporting by region), local advertising coordination (geo-targeted ad budgets by location performance, location extension setup in Google Ads, local inventory ads), and franchise/corporate governance (brand voice standards for local managers, content approval workflow, compliance monitoring, training materials). Provide a reporting dashboard with location ranking tracking, review aggregate scores, and local conversion metrics.

**Expected output:** Multi-location SEO system with governance playbook, review management workflow, and regional performance dashboard
**Pro tip:** A single 1-star review costs a business 30% of potential customers, so a systematic review response protocol within 24 hours is the highest-ROI local marketing investment.

### 1.74 Voice Search Optimization Strategy
**Use case:** Optimize content for voice search queries as adoption of smart speakers and voice assistants grows
**Best for:** SEO managers, content strategists, technical marketers

Act as a voice search optimization specialist. Develop a voice search strategy for [brand/website] targeting [number] voice queries relevant to [industry]. Cover the fundamental differences between typed and voice queries (question-based long-tail queries, conversational phrasing, local intent bias, featured snippet dependency), technical optimization (structured data markup for FAQ, HowTo, LocalBusiness, QAPage schemas, page speed optimization for mobile sub-3-second load, HTTPS and security signals), content strategy (FAQ page creation targeting question-based keywords, natural language content that answers who/what/when/where/why/how queries, featured snippet optimization with direct answers in first [number] words, listicle and step-by-step formats), local voice optimization (Google Business Profile completeness, "near me" query optimization, review schema for voice-visible ratings), and measurement (voice query tracking via Google Search Console query reports, click-through rates from voice devices, branded vs. non-branded voice search trend). Include a competitive voice search gap analysis against [2-3 competitors] showing which voice queries they currently capture.

**Expected output:** Voice search optimization playbook with query targeting framework, technical checklist, and content templates
**Pro tip:** Voice search returns only one answer 90% of the time the featured snippet, so every voice SEO strategy is actually a featured snippet optimization strategy.

### 1.75 Interactive Content Marketing Strategy
**Use case:** Drive engagement and lead generation through interactive content experiences
**Best for:** Content marketers, demand generation managers

Act as an interactive content strategist. Design an interactive content marketing campaign for [brand] targeting [audience] with a goal of [number] leads. Propose [4-5] interactive content formats (assessments/audits, calculators, quizzes, configurators, interactive infographics, branching scenarios, polls/surveys, interactive video) and select the best format based on audience preference and sales cycle stage. Include content concept development (topic selection based on keyword research and customer pain points, question/input design for maximum completion rate, result/personalization logic, design and UX considerations for mobile-first interaction), distribution strategy (social media teasers that show a result sample, email nurture integration, paid media to promote the interactive experience, embedded lead capture gates), lead qualification integration (how interactive responses feed into lead scoring, segmentation, and personalization), and measurement (completion rate, time spent, share rate, lead quality score vs. static content, conversion rate from interactive experience to next step). Provide a production timeline and estimated budget for each format.

**Expected output:** Interactive content campaign brief with format comparison, UX wireframes, and lead integration workflow
**Pro tip:** Interactive content generates 2x conversions of passive content because people trust their own answers more than anything you tell them.

### 1.76 Account-Based Marketing Target Account Selection and Tiering
**Use case:** Identify and prioritize high-value accounts for ABM campaigns
**Best for:** B2B marketers, demand generation teams, sales development reps

Act as an ABM strategist. Build a target account selection and tiering framework for [company] selling [product/service] to [ideal customer profile] with average contract value of [amount]. Include firmographic criteria (industry codes, company size range by employee count/revenue, location, growth rate, funding stage for startups), technographic signals (current tech stack, tools they use that indicate need, integration compatibility), intent signals (job postings relevant to your solution, leadership changes, funding announcements, competitor usage detection via third-party intent data), engagement scoring (past website visits, content downloads, webinar attendance, sales interactions), and tier assignment (Tier 1: [number] accounts with full ABM orchestration, Tier 2: [number] accounts with 1:few programs, Tier 3: [number] accounts with programmatic ABM). Provide a target account list template with ranking score, tier assignment rules, and a quarterly account refresh process that removes churned or disqualified accounts and adds new prospects.

**Expected output:** Account selection framework with scoring rubric, tier assignment rules, and quarterly refresh protocol
**Pro tip:** 80% of ABM program value comes from the top 20% of accounts, so resist the urge to spread resources across too many targets and go deep on the few.

### 1.77 Account-Based Marketing Campaign Orchestration and Personalization
**Use case:** Execute personalized multi-channel campaigns for target accounts
**Best for:** ABM managers, B2B campaign managers

Act as an ABM campaign orchestrator. Design a 90-day multi-channel ABM campaign for [number] Tier 1 target accounts in [industry] selling [product/service]. Include channel tactics (direct mail sequence with [number] touches, personalized video outreach, LinkedIn ads targeted by company and job title, custom content microsites per account, executive dinner/webinar invites with agenda samples, sales-aligned email sequences), personalization depth (account-specific landing pages, pain-point-tailored case studies, research-backed talking points for sales team, competitive positioning against their likely incumbent vendor), sales and marketing alignment workflow (lead routing rules, alert triggers for engagement signals, weekly ABM huddle agenda, shared account notes in CRM), timeline and orchestration (which channels activate at which stage: awareness, engagement, consideration, decision), and measurement (account penetration rate, engagement score by channel, pipeline influenced, revenue closed from target account list). Provide playbook templates for each channel tactic.

**Expected output:** 90-day ABM campaign orchestration plan with channel playbooks and sales alignment workflow
**Pro tip:** A personalized video message to a decision-maker converts at 5x the rate of a generic email, but only when it references something specific to their company or industry.

### 1.78 Micro-Influencer Partnership Program
**Use case:** Build scalable partnerships with micro-influencers for authentic, high-engagement campaigns
**Best for:** Brand marketers, community managers, small business owners

Act as a micro-influencer partnership strategist. Design a scalable program to recruit, manage, and retain [number] micro-influencers (followers between [min] and [max]) in the [niche] space. Include sourcing and discovery methods (hashtag research, platform-native discovery tools, competitor partnership analysis, follower overlap analysis, influencer database tool recommendations), outreach and relationship building (tiered outreach approach from automated to personalized, onboarding flow with welcome package, community guidelines, expectations document, gift delivery), campaign execution (brief templates designed for micro-influencer autonomy, content approval light-touch workflow, affiliate link or discount code setup), compensation model (product seeding, flat fee, commission-based, hybrid options, gifting + performance bonus structure), measurement (engagement rate benchmarks for nano/micro tier, storytelling performance vs. sales performance, long-term partnership retention rate, cost-per-engagement comparison to paid ads), and community building among the micro-influencer network (private group, exclusive previews, co-creation sessions, annual summit or retreat).

**Expected output:** Micro-influencer program playbook with sourcing workflow, partnership tiers, compensation models, and retention strategy
**Pro tip:** Micro-influencers with 5,000-20,000 followers have the highest engagement rates (5-7%) because their audience still feels like a real relationship, not a broadcast channel.

### 1.79 Community-Led Growth Strategy
**Use case:** Build a brand community that drives acquisition, retention, and advocacy
**Best for:** Community managers, growth marketers, B2B SaaS marketers

Act as a community-led growth strategist. Design a community-led growth strategy for [brand/company] targeting [audience]. Include community platform selection criteria (Slack vs. Discord vs. Circle vs. custom platform) based on audience preference, engagement patterns, and integration needs, community structure (public vs. private spaces, topic-based channels vs. open forum, member tiers (new, active, core, ambassador) with permissions and benefits for each), onboarding and activation workflow (welcome sequence, first contribution prompt, [number]-day challenge to drive initial engagement, community buddy system), value creation (exclusive content, expert AMAs, peer support network, job board, co-creation opportunities, member spotlight), growth mechanics (referral program for members, shareable community content, NPS promoter invitation, public community contributions that showcase value), monetization path (freemium community with paid premium tiers, community as retention moat tied to product subscription), and measurement (daily/monthly active members, questions answered within [timeframe], community-sourced leads, retention lift for community members vs. non-members, net promoter score). Include a 90-day launch plan with milestones for each phase.

**Expected output:** Community-led growth strategy with platform selection, activation workflow, growth mechanics, and measurement framework
**Pro tip:** The first 100 members define community culture forever, so recruit them manually and purposefully rather than opening the doors to anyone.

### 1.80 Marketing Compliance and Legal Review Workflow
**Use case:** Ensure all marketing materials comply with regulations without slowing down campaign velocity
**Best for:** Marketing operations managers, in-house counsel, compliance officers

Act as a marketing compliance and legal operations specialist. Design a streamlined compliance review workflow for [company] producing [number] marketing assets per month across [channels]. Cover the key regulatory areas relevant to [industry] (FTC endorsement guidelines for influencer and UGC content, CAN-SPAM and GDPR/CMPR for email marketing, truth-in-advertising standards, industry-specific regulations like HIPAA, FINRA, FDA, or ASA rules, accessibility requirements (WCAG 2.1 AA for digital assets), data privacy restrictions on retargeting and lookalike audiences, copyright and trademark clearance for music, imagery, and user content). Build the workflow as: asset categories by risk level (low: social posts without claims, medium: email campaigns and blog posts, high: advertising copy with health/performance claims, financial projections, testimonials), review routing by risk level (low = self-certify with checklist, medium = one legal reviewer with 24-hour SLA, high = two-person legal review with 48-hour SLA plus senior sign-off), pre-approved language library (claim templates with pre-cleared wording, disclaimer language per channel, disclosure formats for each platform), and version control and archiving (asset tagging by approval ID, compliance audit trail, quarterly content audit for stale claims). Provide a tracking dashboard template and a monthly compliance report format for leadership.

**Expected output:** Compliance review workflow with risk-tiering matrix, SLA framework, pre-approved language library, and audit trail system
**Pro tip:** A pre-approved language library cuts legal review time by 70% because 80% of marketing content uses the same claims and disclaimers repeated across campaigns.

## 2. Content Creation Prompts (70 Prompts)

Prompts for blog posts, articles, newsletters, social media content, scripts, and all forms of digital content creation.

### 2.1 Long-Form Blog Post Architect
**Use case:** Outline and write a comprehensive, research-backed blog post
**Best for:** Content marketers, bloggers, SEO specialists

Act as a senior content strategist and writer who creates blog posts that rank, engage, and convert. I need a comprehensive blog post.

Topic: [blog post topic] | Target keyword: [primary SEO keyword] | Target audience: [who will read this] | Goal: [traffic, leads, authority, sales] | Tone: [professional, conversational, educational, contrarian] | Word count: [desired length] | Key points: [must-include subtopics]

Write a complete blog post. SEO Metadata: Title tag (60 chars) with 3 options. Meta description (160 chars) with 3 options each including primary keyword. URL slug. Focus keyword usage guidance. 5-7 secondary LSI terms. Introduction (200-300 words): Hook (question, statistic, story, bold statement), context, problem statement, thesis, preview. Body (6-10 sections): Each gets an H2 heading, 300-500 words, original insights, examples, transitions, internal links. Mix of: educational explainer, practical how-to, case study, counter-intuitive debunk, comparison or evaluation, expert opinion or research. Conclusion (150-200 words): 3 key takeaways, reinforced main message, clear CTA.

**Expected output:** Complete blog post with all sections, SEO metadata, and linking strategy
**Pro tip:** After writing, check readability targeting grade 8-10 and add 3-5 internal links

### 2.2 LinkedIn Thought Leadership Post
**Use case:** Write high-engagement LinkedIn posts that build authority
**Best for:** Founders, executives, consultants, personal brands

You are a LinkedIn content strategist who has helped executives grow audiences to 100K+ followers. I need a thought leadership post.

Topic or insight: [what I want to share] | My expertise: [what I am known for] | Target audience on LinkedIn: [who I want to reach] | Post goal: [engagement, authority, leads, conversation] | Brand voice: [professional, bold, educational, conversational, contrarian] | Supporting evidence: [data, personal story, case study, observation]

Select the best format: The Contrarian Take, The Personal Story, The How-To, The Framework, The Hot Take, or The List. Write the post with a hook in the first 3 lines (LinkedIn truncates there), 8-15 lines of body using short paragraphs of 1-2 sentences each, and a CTA that drives comments. Use single line returns. Each line should be a complete thought. Add 3-5 hashtags mixing broad, niche, and branded. Include visual recommendation and engagement plan for first 60 minutes including who to tag and how to respond.

**Expected output:** Complete LinkedIn post with format recommendation, full body, and engagement plan
**Pro tip:** LinkedIn algorithm prioritizes posts where people spend time — use compelling line breaks to slow the scroll

### 2.3 Twitter or X Thread Writer
**Use case:** Create engaging Twitter threads that drive followers and engagement
**Best for:** Content creators, founders building audience on X

Act as a Twitter or X content strategist who writes threads that consistently get 10K+ views. I need a compelling thread.

Topic: [thread topic] | Key insight: [the core idea] | Target audience on X: [who will find this valuable] | Format style: [educational, controversial, story-based, tutorial, list] | Tone: [professional, witty, direct, provocative, helpful] | Supporting material: [data, examples, anecdotes]

Write a complete thread of 10-20 tweets. Opening Tweet (The Hook): The most important tweet that determines if people scroll into the thread. Must stand alone and be retweetable. Use curiosity gap, bold claim, surprising data, provocative question, or contrarian view. Thread Structure: Each tweet advances the argument, ends with a hook to the next, is under 240 characters, and includes line breaks. Place media every 3-5 tweets. Follow a narrative arc across the thread: tweets 1-2 hook and setup, 3-7 core insight, 8-12 deeper dive with examples, 13-16 takeaways, 17-18 summary, 19-20 CTA. Final Tweet: Summary, what to do next, retweet ask. Call-to-Engagement: Question to drive replies and quote template.

**Expected output:** Complete Twitter thread with all tweets, visual strategy, and engagement prompts
**Pro tip:** The first tweet is the ONLY tweet most people see — spend 50% of writing time on this one tweet

### 2.4 Email Newsletter Template Pack
**Use case:** Write an entire email newsletter edition with multiple sections
**Best for:** Newsletter writers, content marketers, founders

Act as a newsletter editor who runs a high-performing publication. I need a complete newsletter edition.

Newsletter name: [name] | Topic: [niche or subject] | Audience: [who subscribes] | Format: [curated links, long-form essay, mix, tutorial, interview] | Tone: [casual, professional, witty, educational] | Featured topic: [main content focus] | Secondary items: [tools, resources, links] | Sponsor or affiliate: [if applicable]

Write a complete edition. Subject Line (5 options) using curiosity gap, direct benefit, question, newsjacking, personal, or curiosity formulas. Preheader (5 options) 50-100 characters. Opening Section (From the Editor): Personal note 100-150 words showing personality. Main Content (300-500 words): If essay write full thought piece. If curated provide 3-5 links with 2-3 sentence summaries. If tutorial write step-by-step. Quick Hits (2-4 short items): 2-3 sentences each on tools, articles, books. Community Section: Highlight from last week, upcoming events, reader poll. Sponsor Section: Natural integration with personal experience. Closing: CTA, signature with social links, and PPS (most-clicked section).

**Expected output:** Complete newsletter edition with all sections, subject lines, and preheader options
**Pro tip:** Readers decide to open based on subject line and stay based on the first 100 words

### 2.5 Video Script (60-Second Format)
**Use case:** Write a tight, engaging 60-second video script for Reels, Shorts, or TikTok
**Best for:** Social media content creators, short-form video marketers

You are a short-form video scriptwriter who understands platform-native content. I need a 60-second script.

Topic: [what the video is about] | Target audience: [who will watch] | Platform: [TikTok, Instagram Reels, YouTube Shorts] | Goal: [views, followers, engagement, traffic, sales] | Tone: [educational, entertaining, inspirational, controversial, helpful] | Key message: [the one thing viewers must remember]

Write a complete script with time breakdown. 0:00-0:03 — Hook: pattern interrupt, curiosity gap, bold statement, question, or visual shock. 0:03-0:10 — Setup: context, relatable framing. 0:10-0:45 — Main Content: value in quick segments of no more than 5-7 seconds each. 0:45-0:55 — Application: result, before/after, proof. 0:55-0:60 — CTA: follow, save, comment, share, link in bio. For each segment provide spoken text, on-screen text overlays, visual direction, and audio notes. Include caption system and hashtags.

**Expected output:** Complete 60-second video script with visual directions, captions, and timing
**Pro tip:** Hook within the first 2 seconds or lose 60% of viewers — start with the most interesting moment

### 2.6 Medium Article Draft
**Use case:** Write a complete, publication-ready Medium article
**Best for:** Writers, thought leaders publishing on Medium

Act as a Medium writer who consistently gets featured in top publications. I need a publication-ready article.

Topic: [article topic] | Target audience on Medium: [who will read this] | My expertise: [why I am qualified] | Key message: [the core insight] | Tone: [conversational, authoritative, provocative, personal] | Length: [1000-2000 words]

Write a complete article. Headline (10+ options) using numbered list, how-to, surprising insight, provocative, personal narrative, and question formulas. Subtitle: 1-2 sentences expanding on the headline. Opening Hook (first 150 words): Personal story with twist, surprising statistic, provocative question, vivid scene-setting, or direct challenge. End with thesis. Body: H2 subheadings, bold key phrases, pull quotes, short paragraphs (1-3 sentences), embedded links. Arc: problem, flaw, insight, evidence, application, implication. CTA and Engagement: Clap count ask, comment prompt, follow ask, publication tags. Add hero image recommendation and up to 5 tags.

**Expected output:** Complete Medium article with headline options, full body, and publication strategy
**Pro tip:** Medium algorithm prioritizes reading time — a 7-minute read outperforms a 3-minute read

### 2.7 Pillar Page and Ultimate Guide
**Use case:** Create a comprehensive, SEO-dominating pillar page
**Best for:** Content marketers, SEO specialists

Act as a content strategist specializing in topical authority and pillar page creation. I need a comprehensive pillar page.

Pillar topic: [the broad topic you want to own] | Target keyword: [primary keyword] | Supporting keywords: [LSI and related terms] | Target audience: [who this is for] | Internal resources: [existing content that can link]

Write a complete pillar page. H1 Title: Keyword-optimized, compelling. Introduction (200-300 words), table of contents. Core Content Sections (9-15 sections): Each 300-600 words covering foundational definition, historical context, key components, how-to implementation, common mistakes, tools and resources, case studies, expert opinions, data and research, comparison, FAQ, future trends. Internal Linking Strategy: For each section identify 2-3 existing posts linking TO this page and where this page links OUT. Multimedia: Image suggestions, infographic concept, video embeds, downloadable template, embedded social proof. SEO: FAQ schema JSON-LD, People Also Ask integrations, featured snippet optimization, breadcrumb structure. Conversion Elements: Soft CTA at top, contextual inline CTAs, mid-page lead magnet, hard CTA at bottom.

**Expected output:** Complete pillar page with all sections, linking strategy, and conversion elements
**Pro tip:** Set a quarterly review to add new sections, update statistics, and refresh examples

### 2.8 Instagram Carousel Post Creator
**Use case:** Design and write an engaging multi-slide Instagram carousel
**Best for:** Instagram content creators, social media managers

Act as an Instagram content strategist who creates carousels that get saved and shared. I need a complete carousel.

Topic: [carousel topic] | Target audience: [who will engage] | Goal: [saves, shares, followers, website traffic] | Number of slides: [5-10] | Brand aesthetic: [colors, fonts, style] | Key message: [single takeaway] | Supporting points: [3-7 sub-points]

Create a complete carousel. Cover Slide: Bold, benefit-driven, curiosity-sparking headline with clean central text. Slide Structure: Alternate between educational (one key point per slide under 50 words), story (narrative progression), list (numbered or bulleted), and quote (high visual impact) slides. Each slide must advance the narrative, make sense standalone, include brand elements, and lead to the next slide. Final Slide: Summary and CTA. Caption: First 2 lines compelling, 150-250 words expanding topic, CTA driving engagement. Hashtags: 15-30 relevant. Visual Specs: 1080x1350 recommended, font hierarchy, 3 brand colors max.

**Expected output:** Complete Instagram carousel with all slides, captions, and visual direction
**Pro tip:** Carousels that get the most saves teach something actionable in under 10 slides

### 2.9 Content Repurposing Matrix
**Use case:** Turn one piece of content into 20+ formats across platforms
**Best for:** Content teams, solo creators maximizing output

Act as a content efficiency strategist. I need a repurposing plan for one piece of content.

Original content: [blog, video, podcast, report, or webinar] | Title: [title] | Format: [written, video, audio] | Length: [duration or word count] | Key insights: [3-5 bullet points] | Target platforms: [all active platforms]

Create a repurposing matrix. Tier 1 — Quick (same week): LinkedIn post, Twitter thread (10-15 tweets), Instagram carousel (5-7 slides), email newsletter (500-800 words), 3 short video clips (30-90 seconds). Tier 2 — Medium (1-2 weeks): Podcast episode, YouTube video, infographic, PDF lead magnet, SlideShare. Tier 3 — Deep (2-4 weeks): Mini-course (4-5 emails), case study, guest post, webinar, Quora or Reddit answers. Platform-Specific Notes: Format changes, length adjustments, tone shifts, visual requirements. Scheduling Calendar: Day 1 original publish, Day 2 Twitter and LinkedIn, Day 3 newsletter and carousel, Day 4 video clips, Day 7 podcast, Day 10 YouTube, Day 14 infographic, Day 21 mini-course, Day 30 guest post.

**Expected output:** Complete repurposing matrix with timeline, adaptation notes, and tool recommendations
**Pro tip:** The 20% effort (thread, LinkedIn, newsletter) drives 80% of repurposing value

### 2.10 Storytelling Framework Application
**Use case:** Apply narrative techniques to make business content more engaging
**Best for:** Content creators, founders, anyone telling brand stories

You are a storytelling coach. Apply a narrative framework to my content.

What I want to communicate: [the business topic, insight, or message] | Target audience: [who needs to hear this] | Format: [blog, video, speech, social post, presentation] | Desired outcome: [what I want audience to feel or do] | Personal experience: [authentic story I can share]

Select the best framework. Option A — The Hero's Journey (personal transformation): 12 stages from Ordinary World through Return with the Elixir. Option B — Before/After/Bridge (case studies): Before is visceral pain, After is transformed state, Bridge is the mechanism. Option C — The Mountain Structure (how-to): Base is the goal, Ascent is steps with mini-stories, Summit is achievement, Descent is reflection. Option D — Nested Loops (complex topics): Outer and inner story loops that open and close at different times. Once selected, write the full content using that structure with my specific context.

**Expected output:** Story-driven content piece using the selected framework with rationale
**Pro tip:** The most engaging stories have a moment of tension — do not skip what almost went wrong

### 2.11 Newsletter Content Ideas Generator
**Use case:** Generate a bank of newsletter topic ideas with outlines
**Best for:** Newsletter writers, content planners

Act as a content strategist for email newsletters. I need a batch of content ideas.

Newsletter name: [name] | Topic or niche: [what you write about] | Audience: [who subscribes] | Past popular topics: [3-5 most resonant] | Format: [curated, long-form, hybrid, interview, tutorial] | Frequency: [weekly, bi-weekly, monthly] | Goal: [growth, engagement, monetization, authority]

Generate 20 ideas. 5 Educational: Topics that teach something new. Each with working title, what they will learn, why it matters, subject line hook. 5 Story-Based: Personal experiences. Each with narrative angle, insight, why relatable, vulnerability element. 5 Curated or Resource: Links, tools, books roundups. Each with unifying theme, 5-7 resources with annotations, why valuable. 5 Interactive: Polls, questions, challenges, reader contributions. Each with engagement mechanic, what readers contribute, how you feature input, community building.

**Expected output:** 20 newsletter content ideas across 4 categories with outlines and hooks
**Pro tip:** Mix idea types — too many educational issues feel dry, too many story issues feel unfocused

### 2.12 List Post Creator
**Use case:** Write a high-engagement listicle that drives traffic and shares
**Best for:** Content marketers, blog writers, social media managers

Act as a listicle specialist who writes numbered posts that consistently go viral. I need a comprehensive list post.

Topic: [the list topic] | Angle: [specific take or perspective] | Number of items: [5-25] | Target audience: [who will read] | Tone: [professional, funny, provocative, helpful] | Goal: [traffic, shares, backlinks, authority]

Write a complete list post. Headline: Use formulas like "[Number] [Adjective] Ways to [Outcome] Without [Pain]" or "[Number] [Topic] [Mistakes/Tips] That Will [Result]." Generate 10 options. Introduction (150-200 words): Hook, why they should care, what they will learn, preview. List Items: Each gets a bold descriptive subheading, 150-300 words of substance (original insight, example, data point, story, actionable tip), and visual suggestion. Vary format across items. Conclusion (100-150 words): Overarching theme, most important item to start with, CTA to share or comment.

**Expected output:** Complete list post with headline options, all list items, and conclusion
**Pro tip:** Odd-numbered headlines (7, 9, 11, 13) consistently perform better than even-numbered ones

### 2.13 Interview Question Set Generator
**Use case:** Create thoughtful interview questions for expert interviews or podcasts
**Best for:** Podcasters, journalists, content creators

Act as an interview preparation specialist. I need thoughtful, original questions for an upcoming interview.

Interviewee: [name and background] | Their expertise: [what they are known for] | Interview format: [podcast, video, written Q and A, live stage] | Interview length: [total time] | Audience: [who will read or watch] | Topics to cover: [key areas]

Create 20 questions. 3 Warm-Up: Easy but interesting, reveal personality. 10 Deep-Dive: Explore expertise in depth using "You have said X, but how do you respond to Y?", "What is the biggest misconception?", "Walk me through the moment you realized...", "What did you believe 5 years ago that you now think is wrong?", "What is the hardest lesson you learned?" 3 Audience Questions: What your specific audience wants answered. 2 Rapid-Fire: Best advice received, book that changed thinking, guilty pleasure. 2 Closing: What they wish they were asked, what is next, how to find them. Include follow-up probes for each.

**Expected output:** 20 interview questions across 5 categories with follow-up probes
**Pro tip:** The best questions start with "How" or "What" rather than "Do you" or "Is it true"

### 2.14 Content Calendar Generator
**Use case:** Create a month-long content calendar with themes, topics, and distribution
**Best for:** Content teams, social media managers, solo creators

Act as a content operations manager. I need a complete monthly content calendar.

My business: [name] | My niche: [industry or topic] | Content pillars: [3-5 main themes] | Platforms: [where you publish] | Monthly theme: [if applicable] | Upcoming events: [relevant dates] | Content formats: [blog, video, social, newsletter, podcast] | Posting frequency: [how often per platform]

Generate a 30-day content calendar. Weekly Themes: Assign a theme to each week (Education, Story, Promotion, Community). Daily Breakdown: For each day provide topic, content pillar, format, platform(s), headline hook (3 options), visual direction, posting time, and connection to other content. Content Batching Plan: Group similar types for efficient creation. Repurposing Notes: How each piece flows across platforms. Blog post Monday becomes Twitter thread Tuesday, LinkedIn Wednesday, newsletter Thursday, Instagram carousel Friday.

**Expected output:** Complete 30-day content calendar with daily topics, hooks, and repurposing flow
**Pro tip:** Theme your weeks rather than planning day-by-day — weekly themes create momentum

### 2.15 Comparison Article Writer
**Use case:** Write an unbiased, detailed comparison between two products or approaches
**Best for:** Affiliate marketers, review sites, SaaS content teams

Act as a product review specialist. I need a detailed comparison article.

Product A: [name and description] | Product B: [name and description] | Target audience: [who is comparing] | Primary keyword: [search term like X vs Y] | Reader intent: [what they want to decide] | Affiliate relationships: [if any, disclosure needed]

Write a complete comparison article. Headline: "X vs Y: Which is Better for [Audience] in [Year]?" 5 options. Introduction (150-200 words): Why compare these, key question, quick verdict. Product Overviews: 2-3 paragraphs each on what it is, who it is for, key features, pricing, ideal use case. Comparison Categories: 5-7 categories (ease of use, features, pricing, support, integrations, performance, scalability). Each gets side-by-side analysis, specific evidence, winner for this category, rating. Pricing Comparison: Detailed breakdown with table format. Winner and Recommendation: Overall winner, criteria for when to choose A vs B, specific use cases, final recommendation by user profile. FAQ: 5-7 common questions.

**Expected output:** Complete comparison article with all sections, tables, and final recommendation
**Pro tip:** Be honest about weaknesses — articles that show a product losing in some categories are more trustworthy

### 2.16 How-To Tutorial Script
**Use case:** Write a step-by-step tutorial that teaches a specific skill or process
**Best for:** Educational content creators, software trainers, bloggers

Act as a technical writer and educator. I need a step-by-step tutorial.

Topic: [what you are teaching] | Skill level: [beginner, intermediate, advanced] | Prerequisites: [what they need to know] | Tools needed: [what they need] | Completion time: [how long it takes] | Platform: [blog, video, email, course] | Outcome: [what they will be able to do after]

Write a complete tutorial. Title: Clear, benefit-driven, includes outcome. 5 options. Introduction (100-150 words): What they will learn, why it matters, what they will be able to do, estimated time, prerequisites. Step-by-Step: Each step gets a clear action heading, 2-4 paragraphs with context (why this matters, what to look for, what could go wrong), commands in bold or code, screenshot suggestions, time estimate, and common mistakes. Tips and Best Practices: 3-5 expert tips. Variations: How to customize the process. Troubleshooting: 5-7 common problems with specific solutions. Conclusion: Quick recap, what to learn next, CTA.

**Expected output:** Complete tutorial with all steps, troubleshooting, and best practices
**Pro tip:** Anticipate where people get stuck — include a "if you see this error" note for 3+ common failure points

### 2.17 Viral Content Idea Brainstorm
**Use case:** Generate creative, high-potential content ideas for social media virality
**Best for:** Social media managers, content creators seeking breakout content

Act as a viral content strategist. I need creative ideas that have viral potential.

My brand or niche: [topic or industry] | Target audience: [who should share this] | Platforms: [which platforms] | What worked before: [past high-performing content] | My unique angle: [what makes my perspective different]

Generate 20 ideas. 5 Using Controversy or Debate: Challenge common beliefs. Each includes provocative statement, why it generates comments, how to keep it productive. 5 Using Emotional Story: Evoke strong emotion (awe, inspiration, empathy, humor). Each includes narrative arc, emotional trigger, why it motivates shares. 5 Using Utility: Checklists, templates, frameworks, cheatsheets so useful people save and share. Each includes what makes it useful, format, why saved. 5 Using Trend or Newsjack: Tied to current events. Each includes trend to leverage, timely angle, why attention now. For each idea provide format recommendation, headline or hook, viral potential rationale, distribution strategy, and success metric.

**Expected output:** 20 viral content ideas across 4 patterns with hooks and distribution strategy
**Pro tip:** Viral content usually fails on the first attempt — produce 10 ideas, track which gets traction, double down

### 2.18 White Paper or Report Structure
**Use case:** Structure a data-driven white paper or industry report
**Best for:** B2B marketers, thought leaders, researchers

Act as a white paper author. I need a complete structure for an industry report.

Report topic: [subject] | Research available: [surveys, studies, internal data, expert interviews] | Target audience: [who will download this] | Key finding: [main insight] | Report length: [10-30 pages] | Lead generation goal: [downloads, email captures]

Create a complete structure. Title and Subtitle: Authoritative, specific, data-backed. Executive Summary (1 page): Problem researched, methodology, key findings (3-5 with data), recommendations. Must stand alone. Introduction (2-3 pages): Context, gap in knowledge, research credentials, methodology overview, limitations. Key Definitions. Research Findings (6-10 pages): Organized into thematic sections. Each section includes finding stated clearly, supporting data, analysis, implications, expert commentary. Use data visualizations. Case Studies (2-4 pages): 2-3 real-world examples with before state, intervention, results with data, key lesson. Recommendations (2-3 pages): Actionable, organized by audience segment, prioritized by impact and ease. Conclusion (1 page): Recap, CTA. About the Author and Methodology. References.

**Expected output:** Complete white paper structure with section descriptions and data presentation guidance
**Pro tip:** The executive summary is where most readers stop — write it LAST after you know exactly what the report says

### 2.19 Social Media Caption Variation Set

Write platform-specific captions. LinkedIn (150-300 words): Professional, hook with thought-provoking statement, depth with data, CTA invites discussion, 3-5 hashtags. Instagram (100-220 words): Conversational, short paragraphs with line breaks, emoji appropriate, CTA in last line, 15-30 hashtags in separate block. Twitter or X (under 280 chars): Concise, punchy, one clear thought, designed for engagement, 1-2 hashtags max. TikTok (under 150 chars): Casual, trend-aware, minimal hashtags (3-5). Facebook (80-200 words): Community-oriented, encourages comments, link-friendly. Pinterest (200-300 words): SEO-optimized, keyword-rich first 2 sentences, descriptive, 5-10 hashtags. Include rationale for each platform choice.

**Expected output:** Platform-specific caption variations for 6+ platforms with strategic rationale
**Pro tip:** Do not cross-post identical content — each platform audience has different expectations

### 2.21 Press Release or Announcement Draft
**Use case:** Write a professional press release for a company announcement
**Best for:** PR teams, founders announcing news, marketing teams

Act as a PR professional. I need a press release for an announcement.

Company: [name] | Announcement type: [product launch, funding, partnership, hire, milestone, event] | Key message: [single most important thing] | Supporting details: [specifics] | Quote sources: [executive, partner, customer] | Target publications: [media outlets]

Write a complete press release. Headline: Under 100 characters, grabs attention while factual, includes announcement, company name, key benefit. Subheadline: 1-2 sentences adding context with supporting data point. Dateline: City, State, Date. Lead Paragraph: Answers who, what, when, where, why, how. Most important first. Must stand alone. Body (2-3 paragraphs): Inverted pyramid, supporting details, relevant statistics, market context. Quote from Executive: 1-2 paragraphs adding personality and vision, not repeating facts. Quote from Partner or Customer: Third-party validation. Boilerplate: Standard company description, 2-3 sentences. Media Contact: Name, title, email, phone.

**Expected output:** Complete press release with headline, quotes, and media contact information
**Pro tip:** Journalists receive hundreds of releases daily — your headline must communicate relevance in under 3 seconds

Main Sections (6-12): History or background with milestones and contributors, Core Concepts with fundamental principles and definitions, Types or Categories with classification and examples, Applications or Use Cases with real-world examples, Criticism or Limitations with objective controversies and different perspectives, Current Developments with recent advancements and future outlook, Related Topics and what to read next. Citations: Inline in [bracketed number] format matching references section. References: Numbered list with full URLs. Visual Suggestions.

**Expected output:** Complete encyclopedia-style article with all sections and citations
**Pro tip:** Check every adjective and replace opinion words with facts and attributions

Chapter-by-Chapter: For each major section provide core argument, key quotes (2-3), examples and stories, actionable takeaways. Key Frameworks: Present original models in clear format. Actionable Implementation Guide: How to apply starting today, prioritized steps, recommended sequence. Our Angle: Specific topic, why it fits, fresh perspective. Author Bio: 2-3 sentences, link to website or social. Social Promotion Plan: How you will promote when live.

### 2.29 Content Audit and Gap Analysis
**Use case:** Audit existing content and identify gaps and opportunities
**Best for:** Content teams, SEO specialists, content strategists

Act as a content strategist. I need a content audit framework.

My website: [URL] | My niche: [industry] | Content types: [blog, video, podcast, downloads] | Published pieces: [approximate count] | Primary goals: [traffic, leads, sales, authority] | Target keywords: [if known] | Competitor content: [competitor URLs]

Design an audit process. Audit Dimensions: SEO performance (traffic, rankings, impressions), engagement (time on page, bounce rate, shares), conversion (leads generated, goals completed), content quality (comprehensiveness, accuracy, freshness), business alignment. Scoring: 1-5 for each dimension. Actions: Keep and Optimize (high traffic, high quality), Consolidate (multiple pieces on same topic), Refresh (outdated but high potential), Repurpose (good content in wrong format), Retire (low value, no strategic value), Promote (high quality but underperforming). Gap Analysis: Compare against competitors for each key topic. Identify topics competitors cover that you do not, and vice versa. Identify search queries no one covers well. Prioritization: Matrix of Search Volume vs Difficulty. Quick Wins = high volume, low difficulty. Strategic = high volume, high difficulty. Action Plan: Prioritized list with effort, impact, timeline.

**Expected output:** Complete content audit framework with scoring system and prioritized action plan
**Pro tip:** Focus on top 50 traffic-drivers and bottom 50 performers first, not everything at once

### 2.30 Quote Card or Visual Quote Designer

Contrarian twist on common saying, unexpected truth, empowering statement. 5 Storytelling: 2-4 sentences, mini-insight, opens a thought, hints at larger idea. 5 Action-Oriented: CTA framed as quote, challenges reader, creates cognitive dissonance if they do not act. For each provide exact text, why it resonates, visual layout suggestion, hashtag recommendations (3-5), and caption suggestion. Include visual design brief: font pairing, color palette, background treatment, attribution format, sizing specs per platform.

**Expected output:** 15 original quote card texts with visual design specs for each platform
**Pro tip:** The most shared quotes create a moment of recognition — they articulate what the reader already felt

Act as an infographic content strategist. I need a complete content outline for an infographic.

CTA Section: Bottom section, what viewers do next, URL or QR code. Data Sources: All sources cited with URLs. ### 2.32 Podcast Episode Script (Interview Format)
**Use case:** Write a complete interview podcast script with host introduction, questions, and outro
**Best for:** Podcasters, interview show hosts

Act as a podcast scriptwriter. I need a complete interview episode script.

Podcast name: [your show] | Episode topic: [subject] | Guest: [name and background] | Episode goal: [education, entertainment, inspiration, promotion] | Episode length: [duration] | Audience: [your listener] | Key topics: [discussion points]

Write a complete script. Intro (2-3 minutes): Host opening, topic teaser, why it matters today, guest introduction with credibility, what listeners will learn. Questions (15-25): Segment 1 Background and Context (4-5 questions on how they started, pivotal moment). Segment 2 Deep Dive (8-10 questions exploring core topic with frameworks, insights, actionable advice). Segment 3 Challenges (3-4 questions on what went wrong, lessons learned). Segment 4 Practical Advice (3-4 specific takeaways). Segment 5 Rapid Fire (3-4 quick questions: biggest influence, current obsession, what is next). Outro (2-3 minutes): Key takeaways summary, where to find guest, CTA (subscribe, rate, review), next episode teaser, closing signature. Include transitional phrases and time check notes at 25%, 50%, 75% of duration.

**Expected output:** Complete interview podcast script with timed segments, questions, and transitions
**Pro tip:** Share key questions with the guest beforehand so they can prepare great answers

### 2.33 Content Pillar Repurposing Guide
**Use case:** Deconstruct a content pillar theme into 30+ pieces across formats
**Best for:** Content teams, strategists planning comprehensive campaigns

Act as a content operations director. I need a complete content pillar breakdown.

Pillar theme: [main topic] | Target audience: [who this serves] | Business goal: [traffic, leads, sales, authority] | Formats available: [blog, video, podcast, infographic, social, email, downloadable] | Team capacity: [weekly production capacity] | Timeframe: [rollout duration]

Break down into a complete ecosystem. Pillar Page: The definitive guide, comprehensive, covers entire theme, optimized for main keyword, all other content links back. Cluster Content (10-15 pieces): Deeper dives on subtopics, each targets long-tail keyword, links to pillar page. Social Content Series (15-20): 5 LinkedIn posts, one Twitter thread, 3 Instagram carousels, 5 short-form video scripts, 2-3 infographics. Email Content: Welcome sequence on topic, 3-5 email deep-dive series, newsletter edition. Downloadable Assets: Lead magnet, case study PDF, slide deck. Repurposing Flow: Blog becomes Twitter thread becomes LinkedIn becomes newsletter becomes video. Production Timeline: Week-by-week schedule. Distribution Plan: Where each piece published, promotion schedule, syndication.

**Expected output:** Complete content pillar breakdown with 30+ content pieces across formats and timeline
**Pro tip:** Every piece should be discoverable from the pillar page and every piece should link back to it

### 2.34 Content Brief for SEO Writers
**Use case:** Write a detailed content brief for freelance writers or team members
**Best for:** Content managers, editors, SEO specialists

Act as a content editor. I need a detailed content brief for a specific topic.

Topic: [article topic] | Target keyword: [primary SEO keyword] | Target audience: [who will read] | Content goal: [traffic, leads, authority, conversions] | Competitor articles: [URLs of top-ranking content] | Writer: [name or experience] | Tone: [brand voice]

Write a complete brief. Article Overview: Working title (3 options), target word count, reading level, article type (how-to, listicle, guide, comparison, opinion, case study), key message. Audience Context: Who is searching, what they know, what they want to learn, what question they need answered. Search Intent: Informational, commercial, transactional, or navigational. Keyword Requirements: Primary keyword placement (title, H1, first paragraph, H2, URL), 5-10 secondary keywords, related questions to answer (from People Also Ask). Competitor Analysis: Top 3 competing articles, what they cover well, what they miss, what we can do better. Content Structure: Required H2 and H3 headings, what each section covers, key points, internal linking targets (2-3 URLs), external sources to cite. Writing Guidelines: Required elements, tone examples, formatting, what to avoid. Visual Requirements: Images needed, alt text, sourcing. SEO Metadata: Title tag (under 60 chars) 3 options, meta description (under 160 chars) 3 options, URL slug.

**Expected output:** Complete content brief ready to hand to a writer with all specifications
**Pro tip:** The best briefs explain WHY the article exists and WHO it serves, not just what to write

### 2.35 Content Refresh and Update Strategy
**Use case:** Identify and update outdated content to regain search rankings
**Best for:** Content teams, SEO specialists

Act as a content freshness specialist. I need a strategy to update and refresh existing content.

My website: [URL] | Content to refresh: [specific pages or "top 50 traffic pages"] | Current rankings: [current positions if known] | Target: [improve rankings, increase traffic, update stats] | Content age: [when pieces were published] | Industry change rate: [how fast your field evolves]

Create a content refresh system. Identification: Signals that content needs refresh — traffic decline over 3 months, ranking drops of 3+ positions, outdated statistics or references, broken links, competitor published newer content, changes in search intent for target keyword. Prioritization: Score each piece by traffic potential, ranking opportunity, effort required, and strategic importance. Focus on top 20% of candidates first. Refresh Levels: Level 1 — Light Refresh (30 min per piece): Update statistics, fix broken links, refresh dates, improve meta description, add internal links. Level 2 — Medium Refresh (1-2 hours per piece): Rewrite introduction and conclusion, add new sections (FAQ, examples), improve readability, add visuals, update keyword targeting. Level 3 — Deep Refresh (3+ hours per piece): Complete rewrite, new structure, additional keywords, new data and research, updated examples and case studies, new multimedia. Refresh Cadence: Quarterly review for core pages, bi-annual for cluster content, annual for evergreen. Tracking: Monitor ranking changes after refresh, traffic recovery timeline, and content decay rate to optimize future refresh timing.

**Expected output:** Complete content refresh system with prioritization, levels, and tracking
**Pro tip:** The most cost-effective refresh is updating statistics and dates — it signals freshness to Google with minimal effort

### 2.36 Podcast Show Notes Optimizer

Structure the notes with a compelling summary hook, timestamped highlights with quotable moments, guest bio with social links, resource links mentioned, and a clear CTA. Use a template format that makes episodes scannable while including enough keyword-rich copy for SEO discovery.

**Expected output:** A complete show notes document with summary, timestamped highlights, resources, and SEO metadata
**Pro tip:** Publish show notes on your website 24 hours before the episode drops so search engines index them before you promote the episode

Include a content calendar showing which posts drive growth versus which posts drive paid conversion, and explain how to use Substack's native growth features (recommendations, notes, threads, chat) in sequence.

**Expected output:** A 90-day Substack launch plan with content calendar, conversion strategy, and growth tactics
**Pro tip:** The single fastest way to grow on Substack is strategic recommendation swaps with 5-10 publications in adjacent niches on day one

### 2.38 Newsletter Ad and Sponsorship Copywriter

My newsletter covers [topic], my audience is [subscriber description], my open rate is [percentage], my ad placement is [native/sponsored section/solo email], my sponsor is [brand name] offering [product or discount], and their goal is [clicks, sales, or brand awareness]. Write the ad in my newsletter's natural voice so it does not feel like a disruption. Include a subject line or header that signals sponsored content clearly, a hook that ties the sponsor's offer to a problem my readers actually have, 2-3 sentences of genuine context before the offer, the specific deal or CTA, and a brief disclaimer. Provide 3 variations at different lengths: a 50-word inline mention, a 150-word dedicated placement, and a 300-word solo sponsor takeover.

**Pro tip:** The best performing sponsorships solve a problem your audience already has - turn down sponsors whose product does not genuinely help your readers

### 2.39 Content Personalization Engine at Scale
**Use case:** Create dynamic content variations that adapt to different audience segments without rewriting everything
**Best for:** Content marketers, growth teams, email marketers

Act as a content personalization architect who has built scalable personalization systems for B2B and B2C brands. Help me design a content personalization framework that tailors messages to different segments without multiplying my workload. I create content about [topic], my audience segments include [segment 1, segment 2, segment 3], the key differences between them are [differentiator list], and I distribute through [channels]. Build a modular content system with: a core content template that carries the main message, customizable hooks for each segment based on their primary pain point, tailored statistics or proof points per segment, differentiated CTAs that match each segment's buying stage, and personalization tokens or merge fields for email and web. Show me how to create one piece of content and adapt it for 3-5 segments by changing only 20% of the copy. Include a decision tree for choosing which personalization angle to use based on the segment's awareness level and relationship with the brand.

**Expected output:** A content personalization framework with modular templates, segment overlays, and a decision tree
**Pro tip:** Personalize the hook and the CTA only - changing the middle section confuses the core message and doubles production time

### 2.40 Dynamic Content Variation Generator
**Use case:** Generate multiple versions of the same content piece for different channels, formats, and audience temperatures
**Best for:** Content operations teams, social media managers, multi-channel publishers

Act as a content operations specialist who optimizes content for maximum reach per creation hour. Take one core piece of content I have written and generate variations that feel native to each platform. My core content is about [topic], the original format is [blog post/video/newsletter], the original piece is [paste key section or describe], my target platforms are [list 3-5 platforms], and my audience differs across platforms in these ways [describe differences]. For each platform, rewrite the content with: a platform-native hook that fits the content consumption pattern, adjusted length and structure matching platform norms, tone adaptation (more professional on LinkedIn, more casual on TikTok), format changes (text to bullet points to script to visual description), and a platform-specific CTA. Deliver a content adaptation matrix showing the original piece and each variation side by side so I can see exactly what changed between versions.

**Expected output:** Platform-optimized content variations with an adaptation matrix showing original-to-variant changes
**Pro tip:** Keep the core insight identical across all variations - only the packaging changes. If the insight changes per platform, you are writing different content, not repurposing it

### 2.41 AI-Assisted Content Workflow Designer
**Use case:** Design a human-plus-AI content creation workflow that maintains quality while multiplying output
**Best for:** Content teams, solo creators, marketing departments adopting AI tools

Act as a content operations consultant who has designed AI-assisted workflows for newsrooms and marketing teams. Help me build a systematic workflow where AI handles the heavy lifting and humans focus on strategy, voice, and quality control. I create content about [topic], my current output is [pieces per week], my target output is [pieces per week], my team size is [number], and my current tools are [list tools]. Design a workflow with: a research phase where AI gathers sources, competitor content, and data points while humans define the angle and thesis; an outlining phase where AI generates structural options and humans approve the narrative arc; a drafting phase where AI produces the first pass and humans inject voice, stories, and expertise; a review phase with AI handling grammar, readability, and factual consistency while humans check tone, brand alignment, and strategic accuracy; and a distribution phase where AI generates platform adaptations and humans schedule and engage. Include quality gates at each phase, prompt templates for each AI task, and time estimates comparing the traditional workflow to your new workflow.

**Expected output:** An AI-assisted content workflow with phase-by-phase breakdown, prompt templates, and time savings estimates
**Pro tip:** The biggest mistake is treating AI as a writer instead of a research assistant and first-draft generator - your unique perspective is the value, not the ability to string sentences together

### 2.42 Content Repurposing Matrix Across 10+ Platforms
**Use case:** Systematically transform one piece of cornerstone content into 15+ platform-native assets
**Best for:** Content teams, solo creators, anyone maximizing content ROI

Act as a content repurposing strategist who has built systems turning one piece of content into 50+ assets. Take my cornerstone content and generate a complete repurposing matrix. My core asset is a [blog post/video/podcast/research report] about [topic], it is approximately [word count or duration], and its key sections are [list 3-5 major sections or takeaways]. Build a repurposing matrix with these target formats and platforms: a LinkedIn carousel converting the top 5 insights into a swipeable deck; a Twitter/X thread breaking the main argument into 15-20 tweets with a quote tweet hook; an Instagram carousel with condensed takeaways and visual storytelling; a TikTok or Reel script turning one surprising stat into a 60-second video; an email newsletter summary giving subscribers the TL;DR with a link to the full piece; a Medium article with a rewritten opening and SEO-optimized title; a SlideShare or Slide deck version for professional audiences; a podcast episode outline if I want to record a discussion about it; a short video or Loom summary for internal teams or social; an audio clip or audiogram for social sharing; a quote graphic pack with 5-7 quotable moments; a Reddit post or AMA response derived from the content; a Quora answer using the content's core argument; a guest post pitch adapting the content for another publication; a lead magnet or downloadable checklist version; and a newsletter guest excerpt for cross-promotion. For each format specify the exact content, tone adjustment, optimal length, and posting strategy.

**Expected output:** A complete repurposing matrix with 15+ platform-specific assets derived from one piece of content
**Pro tip:** Repurpose in order of effort - start with the 5-minute adaptations (quote graphics, tweet threads) and only invest in high-effort formats (video, carousel) when the core content is performing well

### 2.43 Thought Leadership Framework Builder
**Use case:** Develop a differentiated thought leadership platform that builds authority and drives business outcomes
**Best for:** Founders, executives, consultants building personal brands

Act as a thought leadership strategist who has positioned executives at Fortune 500 companies and fast-growing startups. Help me build a thought leadership platform that stands out in a crowded market. My area of expertise is [topic or industry], my target audience is [who needs to hear from me], my current credentials or experience include [background highlights], my business goal is [lead generation, speaking bookings, book deal, etc.], and my top competitors in this space are [names]. Develop a thought leadership framework with: a point-of-view statement that distills your unique belief about the industry in one sentence (the thing you believe that others do not); 5 pillar topics where you will build authority with a content angle for each; the contrarian stance or debate you are willing to start; your evidence arsenal (original data, case studies, personal experience, frameworks); the content formats that fit your strengths and audience preferences; your publishing rhythm across platforms; and a 90-day content plan showing how each piece connects to the POV and business goal. Also include a "reaction playbook" for responding to industry news and competitor content in a way that reinforces your position.

**Expected output:** A thought leadership platform with POV statement, pillar topics, evidence arsenal, and 90-day content plan
**Pro tip:** True thought leadership requires a point of view that SOME people will disagree with - if everyone nods along, your content is useful but not memorable

### 2.44 Executive Content Ghostwriter
**Use case:** Write content that sounds exactly like a busy executive while maintaining authority and approachability
**Best for:** Ghostwriters, executive assistants, marketing teams supporting executive thought leadership

Act as an executive ghostwriter who has written on behalf of CEOs, founders, and industry leaders across LinkedIn, Twitter, and major publications. Help me produce content that sounds authentically like the executive I am writing for. The executive is [name and title] from [company], their industry is [sector], their natural speaking style is [formal/casual/technical/inspirational], their core expertise is [topic], their key message they want to be known for is [message], their target audience is [followers, peers, potential clients], and their time commitment is [minutes per week they can spend]. Create a batch of content with: 3 LinkedIn posts using their authentic voice (not a polished marketer's voice), 2 Twitter or short-form takes on industry news, 1 newsletter or long-form piece covering their perspective on a trend, and a 2-sentence bio that conveys authority without being arrogant. For each piece include the talking points you used so the executive can review and approve quickly. Build a voice guide document capturing their preferred phrases, topics they avoid, storytelling patterns they favor, and examples of what sounds like them versus what does not.

**Expected output:** A batch of ghostwritten content pieces plus a voice guide document for ongoing consistency
**Pro tip:** Record 15 minutes of the executive speaking naturally in a conversation or interview, and use that transcript as your voice reference - written communication is usually more formal than speech, and speech is what feels authentic

### 2.45 Data-Driven Storyteller
**Use case:** Transform raw data and statistics into compelling narratives that audiences remember and share
**Best for:** Content marketers, data journalists, analysts presenting findings to non-technical audiences

Act as a data storyteller who specializes in turning complex data into narratives that drive action. I have data I want to turn into content, and I need you to find the story hidden in the numbers.
