My dataset or research covers [topic], the key finding is [main insight], the data source is [source name], the target audience is [who needs to understand this], the business goal is [awareness, authority, lead generation, or behavior change], and I want to publish on [platform or format]. First, help me identify the narrative arc hidden in the data by analyzing what surprised you most, what challenges common assumptions, what reveals a trend or pattern, and what suggests a clear action. Then structure the story with: a headline that includes the most surprising or actionable number; a hook that frames the data as answering a question the audience already has; 3-5 data-driven insights each presented as a claim supported by the number, the context that makes it meaningful, and the implication for the audience; a visual concept for each data point (chart type, what to emphasize, color scheme); and a conclusion that answers "so what" and gives the audience something to do with this information. Include original analogies or metaphors that make abstract numbers feel concrete.

**Expected output:** A complete data story structure with narrative arc, data points with context, visual concepts, and audience takeaways
**Pro tip:** The most shareable data stories challenge a widely held belief - find the number that contradicts what everyone assumes is true

### 2.46 Content for Sales Enablement
**Use case:** Create content assets that directly support sales conversations and shorten the sales cycle
**Best for:** Content marketers, sales enablement managers, B2B marketing teams

Act as a sales enablement content strategist who has built content libraries that sales teams actually use. I need content that helps my sales team close deals faster. My product is [product or service], my ICP is [ideal customer profile], the average deal size is [amount], the sales cycle is [duration], top objections are [objection list], and my current win rate is [percentage if known]. Design a sales enablement content library with: a battle card for each top competitor covering their positioning, our counter-arguments, and proof points; a one-pager for each stage of the buyer's journey (awareness, consideration, decision); a ROI calculator or value framework the sales team can use in conversations; case studies organized by use case, industry, and deal size with the exact data points sales should highlight; objection handling one-pagers for the top 5 objections with scripts and proof points; an executive summary document that C-level buyers can read in 3 minutes; a technical deep-dive for procurement or IT evaluation; and a competitive displacement document for taking deals from the incumbent. For each asset specify how the sales team should use it, in which meeting, and what to say when sharing it.

**Expected output:** A sales enablement content library with battle cards, case studies, objection handlers, and usage guidelines
**Pro tip:** The best sales content is created AFTER talking to sales reps about what actually works in calls, not before - reverse engineer their winning conversations into content

### 2.47 Newsletter Welcome Sequence Architect
**Use case:** Design a multi-email welcome sequence that converts new subscribers into engaged readers and customers
**Best for:** Newsletter operators, email marketers, content creators

Act as an email welcome sequence specialist who has designed onboarding flows for newsletters with millions of subscribers. I need a welcome sequence that turns new subscribers into habitual readers who open every email. My newsletter covers [topic], my target subscriber is [persona], my lead magnet or free offer is [what they signed up for], I send newsletters at [frequency], and my monetization model is [free/paid/sponsored/mixed]. Design a 5 to 7 email welcome sequence with: an immediate confirmation email that delivers the lead magnet and sets expectations for what and when they will hear from you; a "who am I and why this newsletter" email sharing your origin story and what makes your perspective unique; a "best of" email showcasing your 3 most popular past editions so they see the value fast; a "what to expect" email establishing the regular content rhythm and any features or segments you offer; an engagement email asking them to reply with their biggest challenge or question; a social connection email inviting them to follow you on other platforms or join a community; and an offer email (if monetized) introducing your paid tier or product with a subscriber-only discount. For each email provide subject line (3 options), preview text, body copy designed for skimming, and the specific goal of that email in the sequence.

**Expected output:** A complete newsletter welcome sequence with 5-7 emails, subject lines, and strategic rationale per email
**Pro tip:** Your welcome sequence should deliver more value than expected in the first 3 emails - over-delivering upfront builds the habit of opening before you ever ask for anything

### 2.48 Content Performance Dashboard Designer
**Use case:** Build a content performance measurement system that connects content activity to business results
**Best for:** Content marketers, marketing operations, editors

Act as a content analytics specialist who has built performance dashboards for publishing teams and marketing departments. Help me design a content performance dashboard that shows which content actually drives business outcomes. My content operation produces [types of content], across [channels], my primary business goal is [leads, traffic, sales, subscribers, or engagement], my analytics tools are [Google Analytics, Content management system, social platforms], and my team reports to [stakeholder names]. Design a dashboard with: a top-level section showing content contribution to business goals (leads attributed, revenue influenced, traffic to conversion pages); an engagement section showing time on page, scroll depth, social shares, comments, and email click-throughs by piece; a content efficiency section showing production cost per piece, time spent, and performance per hour invested; a channel comparison showing which distribution channels drive the most engaged traffic; a content audit section flagging underperforming pieces that need updates and top performers that should be repurposed; a trend section showing performance over time with seasonality markers; and a recommendations engine section that lists specific actions based on the data (update this, repurpose that, retire this). For each metric include the definition, calculation method, benchmark if available, and a decision rule (what to do when this metric moves up or down).

**Expected output:** A content performance dashboard design with metric definitions, benchmarks, and action recommendations for each section
**Pro tip:** Track the same metrics for 90 days before making major changes - content performance has natural variance and reacting too early leads to wrong conclusions

### 2.49 Content Localization and Adaptation Strategy
**Use case:** Adapt content for international audiences while preserving brand voice and cultural relevance
**Best for:** Growth marketers, international expansion teams, content ops managers

Act as a content localization strategist who has helped brands enter 10+ international markets without losing their voice. I need a strategy for adapting my content for new geographic or cultural audiences. My brand is [brand name], my core content is about [topic], my current market is [home market], my target markets are [list 2-4 new markets], my content types are [blog, social, email, video], and my localization budget and resources are [translation service, in-country team, or DIY]. Design a content localization framework with: a prioritization matrix for which markets to enter first based on content demand, language overlap, and cultural distance; a localization depth model for each market (translation only, adaptation with local examples, or full recreation with local creators); a glossary of brand terms, idioms, and voice elements that must be handled carefully per market; a cultural sensitivity checklist covering symbols, colors, humor styles, references, and taboos for each target market; a content calendar showing how to sequence localization efforts to maximize efficiency; a quality assurance process including in-country review, back-translation checks, and A/B testing localized versus original versions; and measurement guidelines for tracking performance per market with local benchmarks.

**Expected output:** A content localization strategy with market prioritization, adaptation depth model, cultural checklist, and QA process
**Pro tip:** Never lead with translation - lead with cultural adaptation. A perfectly translated piece that uses the wrong local references will underperform a moderately translated piece that feels locally relevant

### 2.50 Top-of-Funnel Content Magnet Creator
**Use case:** Create awareness-stage content that attracts new audiences and starts the relationship
**Best for:** Content marketers, growth teams, brand marketers

Act as a top-of-funnel content strategist who specializes in attracting cold audiences and turning them into subscribers or followers. I need content that brings new people into my ecosystem. My brand offers [product or service], my ideal audience profile is [persona description], their top 3 unaware problems are [problems they have not yet named], my distribution channels are [channels], and my TOFU content goal is [traffic, subscribers, social followers, or brand impressions]. Create a TOFU content magnet plan with: 3 educational content ideas that address problems the audience knows they have (not your product's solution); 3 entertaining or curiosity-based content ideas that stop the scroll and build brand recall; 3 thought leadership or contrarian takes that position your brand as having a unique perspective; for each idea include the title, hook, format recommendation, distribution channel, what makes it shareable, and the conversion path (what action should they take after consuming this). Include a headline framework for TOFU content that optimizes for curiosity and search discovery, and guidance on how much product mention is appropriate at each awareness level.

**Expected output:** 9 TOFU content ideas with headlines, formats, distribution channels, and conversion paths for each
**Pro tip:** TOFU content should answer the question the audience is ALREADY searching for, not the question you wish they were asking - use search data to validate demand before writing

### 2.51 Middle-and-Bottom-of-Funnel Content Converter
**Use case:** Create consideration and decision-stage content that moves prospects toward purchase
**Best for:** Content marketers, demand generation teams, B2B marketers

Act as a conversion-focused content strategist who builds BOFU content that drives pipeline and revenue. I need content that persuades prospects who know their problem to choose my solution. My product is [product or service], my typical buyer considers [competitors], the top 3 decision criteria are [criteria], the main objections are [objections], the average deal size is [amount], and the sales cycle is [duration]. Create a MOFU and BOFU content library with: 3 comparison content pieces (versus competitor, versus doing nothing, versus building in-house) each with a balanced framing that makes your solution the logical choice; 3 case studies structured as before-after-bridge with specific metrics and the moment of "aha" for the customer; 2 implementation or onboarding guides that reduce perceived risk by showing exactly what happens after purchase; 1 ROI calculator or value framework the prospect can use to justify the decision internally; 1 FAQ or objection-handling guide addressing every concern that comes up in late-stage conversations; and 1 evaluation checklist or RFP template that helps the prospect compare options and positions your strengths as must-haves. For each asset specify where it lives in the buyer's journey, who should share it (sales or marketing), and what to say when presenting it.

**Expected output:** A MOFU/BOFU content library with comparison pieces, case studies, ROI tools, and objection handlers
**Pro tip:** BOFU content should answer questions the prospect is afraid to ask - money, risk, implementation nightmares, and the real reason past solutions failed. Address those openly and you win trust

### 2.52 Content Distribution Partnerships Playbook
**Use case:** Build strategic partnerships that amplify your content reach without paid distribution
**Best for:** Content marketers, growth teams, partnership managers

Act as a content distribution partnerships specialist who has built cross-promotion networks reaching millions of readers. I need a partnership strategy to multiply my content reach. My brand creates content about [topic], my audience size is [subscribers, followers, or traffic], my content types are [blog, newsletter, video, podcast], my ideal partner profile is [complementary brand or creator with similar audience], and my distribution goal is [reach new readers, grow email list, or build backlinks]. Build a partnership playbook with: a partner identification framework including where to find them, how to evaluate audience overlap, and how to prioritize by potential reach; 4 partnership models with templates: content swap (cross-publish each other's content), guest content exchange (write for each other's channels), co-created content (joint research, webinar, or series), and reciprocal promotion (share each other's content with a personal endorsement); an outreach sequence for each partnership type including the initial message, value proposition, and follow-up; a co-marketing agreement template covering deliverables, timelines, promotion commitments, and success metrics; a tracking system for measuring reach, engagement, and new subscribers per partnership; and a tiered partnership management approach (casual, regular, strategic) with escalation criteria. Include a 30-day action plan for setting up 5 initial partnerships.

**Expected output:** A content distribution partnerships playbook with partner identification, outreach templates, partnership models, and a 30-day launch plan
**Pro tip:** The best partnership outreach mentions the partner's content by name and explains why your audiences overlap - generic "let's collaborate" messages get ignored

### 2.53 Discussion-Based Content Strategist
**Use case:** Create interactive content formats that spark conversations and drive engagement on social platforms
**Best for:** Social media managers, community builders, thought leaders

Act as a social engagement strategist who specializes in generating meaningful discussions through interactive content. I need content that starts conversations rather than broadcasting messages. My brand or profile operates in [industry], my audience on [LinkedIn/Twitter/LinkedIn] consists of [follower description], my content goal is [engagement, brand awareness, community building], and topics I can talk about are [topic list]. Create a discussion-based content plan with: 5 LinkedIn poll ideas with the poll question, answer options designed to reveal insights, the follow-up post you will write after seeing poll results, and how to use the data in future content; 3 Twitter Space or LinkedIn Audio event concepts with the format (interview, panel, AMA, debate), the hook topic that encourages attendance, ideal speakers or co-hosts, and promotion strategy; 5 opinion or debate-style posts that take a clear stance (not vague enough for everyone to agree) and include a specific ask for disagreement in the comments; 3 "fill in the blank" or "which one" interactive post formats that are easy to engage with; 2 question-based posts that ask for specific advice or experience sharing rather than generic opinions; and a community response strategy for how to reply to comments in a way that extends the conversation (not just "great point!"). Include engagement benchmarks per format so you know what "working" looks like.

**Expected output:** A discussion-based content plan with polls, audio events, opinion posts, and a comment response strategy
**Pro tip:** The most engaging posts intentionally leave something OUT - a controversial take, an unanswered question, or an incomplete list - because people engage to complete the thought

### 2.54 Micro-Content and Atomic Essay Writer
**Use case:** Distill complex ideas into ultra-concise content that respects readers' limited attention
**Best for:** Twitter/X creators, LinkedIn writers, newsletter editors, anyone practicing short-form mastery

Act as a brevity-focused writer who has mastered the art of saying more with fewer words. I need help condensing my ideas into micro-content that delivers full value in seconds. My core idea or insight is [idea], my target platform is [Twitter/X, LinkedIn, Instagram, or short-form platform], my audience is [who needs to hear this], my typical post length is [current character count], and my goal is [engagement, shares, or thought leadership]. Apply the atomic essay framework: distill the core insight to one sentence that could stand alone; expand to a 3-sentence version (hook, insight, takeaway); write a full atomic essay (150-250 words) with a strong opening line, one main idea supported by one specific example or data point, and a memorable closing line. Then compress it further: a single paragraph version (50-80 words), a Twitter thread version (15-20 tweets with a quote tweet hook), and a quote-card version (one sentence designed to be shared as a graphic). Include your editing notes showing what you cut and why, so I learn to be more ruthless with my own editing. Provide a checklist of words and phrases that can almost always be removed without losing meaning.

**Expected output:** A micro-content family with atomic essay, tweet thread, quote cards, and editing rationale
**Pro tip:** Write the full version first and then cut ruthlessly - you cannot edit a blank page, but you can always cut 50% from a first draft without losing substance

### 2.55 Multimedia Content Planning Framework
**Use case:** Plan and coordinate multimedia content projects that combine text, video, audio, and visuals
**Best for:** Content teams, media producers, marketing departments

Act as a multimedia content producer who has managed cross-format content projects for media brands and agencies. I need to plan a content project that spans multiple formats and media types. My content topic is [topic], my target audience is [description], the formats I want to include are [text, video, audio, infographic, interactive], my production resources are [team size, tools, budget], my distribution channels are [channels], and my timeline is [deadline]. Design a multimedia content plan with: a content architecture showing how each format supports and cross-links to the others (for example, the video summarizes, the article deep-dives, the infographic visualizes, the podcast discusses); a production sequence showing which piece gets created first and how each subsequent piece builds on the previous one (typically text first, then visual, then video, then audio); a format-specific brief for each asset including the angle, key points, format constraints, and distribution path; a cross-promotion plan showing how each asset promotes the others with specific CTAs and links; a asset management system for storing and organizing raw files, drafts, final versions, and distribution copies; a timeline with dependencies showing which pieces block others; and success metrics per format with the understanding that different formats will perform differently and that is okay.

**Expected output:** A multimedia content plan with format architecture, production sequence, briefs per asset, and cross-promotion strategy
**Pro tip:** Produce the text version first even if video is your primary format - writing clarifies your argument faster than recording and editing does

### 2.56 Newsletter Segmentation Strategist
**Use case:** Design audience segments and targeted content tracks that increase engagement and conversion
**Best for:** Newsletter operators, email marketers, Substack and Revue creators

Act as an email segmentation specialist who has built targeted newsletter programs for audiences from 1,000 to 500,000 subscribers. Help me design a newsletter segmentation strategy that sends the right content to the right subscribers. My newsletter covers [topic], I currently have [subscriber count], my current send style is [one-size-fits-all/multi-track], my engagement metrics are [open rate and click rate], my subscriber data includes [signup source, topic preferences, paid status, engagement history], and my goals are [higher open rates, better conversion, reduced unsubscribes]. Design a segmentation strategy with: a segmentation model identifying 3-5 meaningful ways to group subscribers (by interest topic, by engagement level, by signup source, by paid status, by content format preference); for each segment, a content track explaining what they receive, how often, and why it fits them; a re-engagement and win-back plan for cold subscribers including a sunset policy for non-openers after [X] days; an upgrade path showing how subscribers move from one segment to another as their engagement deepens; the technical implementation steps in common email platforms (ConvertKit, Mailchimp, Substack, Beehiiv); a testing plan to validate that segmentation actually improves metrics with a before-and-after comparison framework; and an ethical and privacy checklist ensuring segmentation does not cross into creepy personalization.

**Expected output:** A newsletter segmentation strategy with segment definitions, content tracks, technical setup, and validation plan
**Pro tip:** Start with just 2 segments (engaged vs cold) and only add more when you have the content capacity to serve each segment consistently - under-resourced segmentation hurts everyone

### 2.57 Content for Community Platforms (Discord, Slack, Circle)
**Use case:** Create content strategies and formats specifically designed for community-based platforms
**Best for:** Community managers, brand builders, course creators

Act as a community content strategist who has built engaged communities on Discord, Slack, and Circle. I need a content approach that works for community platforms, not broadcast channels. My community is called [community name], it lives on [Discord/Slack/Circle], it serves [audience description], it has [number of members], my role is [community manager/founder/moderator], and the community purpose is [support, education, networking, or paid membership]. Design a community content strategy with: a content calendar balancing scheduled content (weekly threads, AMAs, workshops) with responsive content (answering questions, celebrating wins, facilitating connections); 5 content formats that work specifically in community platforms like icebreaker prompts, weekly discussion threads, member spotlight features, feedback requests, and live events or office hours; a participation architecture showing the path from lurker to active member to contributor, with content triggers at each stage; a moderation and tone guide for how content should be presented to encourage replies and discussion rather than passive consumption; a content recycling plan for your best broadcast content re-framed as community discussion starters; a metrics framework measuring not just posts but replies, reactions, member-initiated threads, and the ratio of staff-to-member content; and a system for surfacing and amplifying the best member-generated content.

**Expected output:** A community content strategy with platform-native formats, participation architecture, and engagement metrics
**Pro tip:** In community platforms, the best content is often the shortest - a well-framed question generates more discussion than a well-written post

### 2.58 Narrative Journalism Style Creator
**Use case:** Apply narrative journalism techniques to create immersive, story-driven content that hooks readers
**Best for:** Long-form writers, brand journalists, content creators focused on storytelling

Act as a narrative journalist who has written feature stories for major publications. Apply narrative journalism techniques to my topic so it reads like a story, not a report. My content topic is [topic or event], my raw material is [interviews, data, personal experience, or research], my target publication or platform is [outlet], my target reader is [description], and the central tension or question I want to explore is [what keeps the reader turning pages]. Transform this material using narrative journalism techniques: open with a scene or moment that drops the reader into the action (not background or context); introduce a central character the reader will care about (or a human lens for abstract topics); build tension through an open question or unresolved conflict that carries through the piece; use short scenes and specific details instead of general descriptions and summaries; include dialogue and quotes that reveal character and advance the story; use pacing variation (short punchy paragraphs alternating with longer descriptive passages); weave context and background in only where the reader needs it to understand the unfolding story; end with a closing that echoes the opening and resolves the central tension or question. Write a full outline using this structure, then write the opening 300 words in narrative style alongside the opening 300 words in standard blog style so I can see the difference.

**Expected output:** A narrative journalism outline, an opening scene, and a side-by-side comparison with standard blog writing
**Pro tip:** Narrative journalism starts with the most interesting moment, not the beginning - find the scene where the tension peaked and start there, then go back and fill in what led to it

### 2.59 Content for Generational Audiences
**Use case:** Adapt content tone, format, and distribution for Gen Z, Millennials, Gen X, and Boomer audiences
**Best for:** Multi-generational brands, content strategists, social media teams

Act as a generational marketing specialist who understands how each age cohort consumes, shares, and acts on content. I need to create content that resonates across generational lines. My brand is [brand name], my industry is [sector], my content topic is [topic], and my target generations are [select from Gen Z, Millennials, Gen X, Boomers]. For each generation, provide: the content format they prefer for this topic (short-form video, long-form text, audio, infographic, community discussion); the optimal length and time commitment for the format; the tone that resonates (direct and authentic for Gen Z, value-driven and efficient for Millennials, credible and respectful for Gen X, authoritative and clear for Boomers); the platforms where they are most receptive to this content; the hook style that stops their scroll (relatable humor for Gen Z, practical shortcut for Millennials, proven methodology for Gen X, established wisdom for Boomers); the CTA that motivates them (participate for Gen Z, optimize for Millennials, verify for Gen X, trust for Boomers); examples of brands doing this well for each generation; the content mistakes that turn off each generation; and a cross-generational content calendar showing how the same core message gets delivered differently to each cohort. Include a decision framework for when to create separate content versus one piece that works across generations.

**Expected output:** A generational content playbook with format, tone, platform, and CTA recommendations for each age cohort
**Pro tip:** Millennials and Gen Z value AUTHENTICITY over polish - highly produced content can actually hurt credibility with these cohorts, while raw, imperfect content builds trust

### 2.60 Content Batching and Production Workflow
**Use case:** Design a systematic content batching system that maximizes output while minimizing context-switching
**Best for:** Solo creators, content teams, anyone scaling content production

Act as a content production manager who has built batching systems producing 30+ pieces of content per week. Help me design a content batching workflow that fits my schedule. I create content about [topic], my formats are [list formats], my current output is [pieces per week], my desired output is [pieces per week], my available creation time is [hours per week], and my biggest bottleneck is [ideation, writing, editing, design, or distribution]. Design a batching system with: a weekly production schedule with dedicated time blocks for each activity type (research, writing, editing, design, distribution) and explanation of why grouping similar tasks improves speed; a monthly ideation session template that generates 30+ content ideas in one sitting using structured prompts; a content template or swipe file system for each format so you never start from blank; a editing workflow specifying how many rounds of revision each piece gets and who does what; a distribution checklist for each piece that takes minutes instead of hours; a queue management system showing how to prioritize which pieces get created in which order; buffer time allocation for timely or reactive content; and a weekly review process to measure output against goals and adjust the system. Include time-saving estimates showing how much faster batching is compared to creating one piece at a time.

**Expected output:** A content batching system with weekly schedule, ideation process, templates, and queue management
**Pro tip:** The biggest time gain comes from separating CREATION from EDITING by at least 24 hours - write everything first, then edit everything in a separate session. Your editing speed doubles when you are not also creating

### 2.61 Content for Voice Search and Audio Platforms
**Use case:** Optimize content for voice search queries and create audio-native content for platforms like Spotify and Amazon Music
**Best for:** SEO specialists, podcasters, audio content creators

Act as a voice search and audio content strategist who understands how people search and consume content differently through voice. I need to adapt my content for voice search and audio-first platforms. My brand is [brand name], my primary content is about [topic], my target keywords include [keyword list], my audio platform targets are [Spotify, Apple Podcasts, Amazon Music, smart speakers], and my current content format is [text/video]. Design a voice and audio content strategy with: a voice search optimization guide covering natural language question phrases (how, what, why, when queries), featured snippet targeting structure, and the conversational keyword phrases people use when speaking versus typing; an audio content adaptation framework for turning written content into listenable audio including sentence length adjustments, signposting language, verbal cues for structure, and pacing recommendations; a show notes format optimized for both human readers and voice discovery algorithms; a platform-specific strategy for each audio platform including description templates, category selection, and metadata optimization; a transcription optimization approach that makes audio content discoverable in text search; and a measurement framework for audio content (completions, skip rates, and search discovery). Include examples of written content rewritten for audio consumption with side-by-side comparison.

**Expected output:** A voice search and audio content strategy with optimization guides, adaptation frameworks, and platform-specific tactics
**Pro tip:** Voice search queries are 3-4 times longer than typed queries and almost always in question format - build content around direct answers to full questions, not keyword phrases

### 2.62 Interactive Content Creator
**Use case:** Design quizzes, calculators, assessments, and tools that engage users and collect first-party data
**Best for:** Content marketers, growth teams, product marketers

Act as an interactive content specialist who has created quizzes, calculators, and assessments that drive 10x engagement over static content. I need an interactive content concept that attracts, engages, and converts my target audience. My brand is [brand name], my audience is [description], my product or service helps with [problem or outcome], my content goal is [leads, data collection, engagement, or brand awareness], and my technical resources are [developer support available, no-code tools only, or existing platform]. Design an interactive content concept with: a format recommendation (personality quiz, knowledge assessment, ROI calculator, interactive infographic, configuration tool, or challenge) with rationale based on audience and goal; the user experience flow from entry to completion to result with the emotional arc at each step; the data collection points and what each tells you about the user; the result or output the user receives and how to make it shareable; the lead capture integration point and what incentive justifies the email address; the segmentation data you can use after the interaction for follow-up content; the promotion strategy including social sharing mechanics, embed opportunities, and partnership distribution; and success benchmarks for completion rate, share rate, and conversion rate for this type of interactive content. Include a brief creative brief ready to hand to a designer or developer.

**Expected output:** An interactive content concept with user flow, data strategy, promotion plan, and creative brief
**Pro tip:** Interactive content completion rates drop by 50% for each additional question beyond 7 - shorter interactions get shared more and have higher completion rates

### 2.63 Podcast Guesting Content Strategy
**Use case:** Create a content system around podcast appearances that multiplies the value of each guest spot
**Best for:** Founders, authors, experts promoting themselves or their business

Act as a podcast guesting strategist who has booked and optimized appearances for dozens of experts across 200+ podcast episodes. I need a system for turning every podcast appearance into long-term content value. My expertise is [topic], my target podcasts reach [audience description], my product or service is [offer], and my core message is [the one thing I want listeners to remember]. Design a podcast guesting content system with: an episode promotion content kit including 5 social posts (pre-episode teaser, live announcement, quote graphic, key takeaway post, episode recap), an email draft to my list, and a story or reel template; a content repurposing workflow for turning the interview into a blog post (transcript to article), a Twitter thread (key quotes and insights), a LinkedIn post (the main thesis), an Instagram carousel (top 5 takeaways), a newsletter edition (TL;DR and link), and a YouTube video (with timestamps and chapters); a guesting tracker spreadsheet template with podcast name, episode link, air date, promotion actions taken, and leads or traffic attributed; a growth loop connecting each appearance to the next (mention a story on one podcast that makes listeners want to hear you on another); and a measurement framework for tracking podcast ROI beyond vanity metrics (listener actions, website visits, followers gained, direct inquiries). Include a "golden line" identification process for finding the 30-second clip worth turning into standalone content.

**Expected output:** A podcast guesting content system with promotion kit, repurposing workflow, tracker template, and ROI framework
**Pro tip:** Record every podcast appearance on your end (Zoom, QuickTime, or audio recorder) so you own the raw file - you can then clip, repurpose, and share without depending on the host to publish

### 2.64 Internal Linking Strategy for Content
**Use case:** Design an internal linking architecture that distributes authority and improves SEO across your content library
**Best for:** SEO content managers, website owners, content editors

Act as an SEO content architect who specializes in internal linking structures that boost page authority and improve user navigation. I need an internal linking strategy for my content library. My website is [URL], I have approximately [number] content pages, my content pillars are [pillar topics], my most important pages for business goals are [key pages], my current internal linking approach is [ad-hoc, category pages only, no system], and my content management system is [platform]. Design an internal linking strategy with: a pillar-to-cluster linking architecture showing how pillar pages link to cluster content and cluster content links back to pillars; a content hierarchy identifying tier 1 (cornerstone), tier 2 (supporting), and tier 3 (news or timely) content with linking rules for each tier; an anchor text strategy covering when to use exact match, partial match, branded, and generic anchor text with a target distribution ratio; a page-specific linking plan for the top 10 most important pages showing which pages should link to each and with what anchor text; a orphan content audit process for finding pages with zero internal links and a plan to integrate them; a link maintenance process for updating links when content is moved, consolidated, or retired; and a measurement framework tracking link equity distribution, crawl depth, and link count per page with targets. Include a one-month implementation plan prioritizing high-impact quick wins.

**Expected output:** An internal linking strategy with link architecture, anchor text guidelines, page-level plans, and audit process
**Pro tip:** No page on your site should be more than 3 clicks from the homepage - pages buried deeper rarely get crawled or indexed, making your internal linking structure a visibility ceiling for all your content

### 2.65 Visual Content Strategy and Planning
**Use case:** Plan a visual content system that supports your brand identity and improves content performance
**Best for:** Visual content creators, brand managers, social media teams

Act as a visual content strategist who has designed visual identity systems for content brands and media companies. I need a visual content strategy that makes my content recognizable and shareable. My brand is [brand name], my brand colors and fonts are [or I need recommendations], my content types are [blog, social, video, email], my platforms are [platform list], my current visual approach is [consistent/inconsistent/nonexistent], and my design resources are [in-house designer, tools like Canva, or outsourced]. Design a visual content strategy with: a visual identity system including color palette (primary, secondary, accent), typography (headline, body, accent fonts), graphic elements (shapes, patterns, icons), and photography or illustration style with examples; a template library specification for each content type (social posts, blog featured images, email headers, quote cards, presentation decks, video thumbnails) with layout, element placement, and sizing guidelines; a content-to-visual pairing framework showing which visual type works best for which content goal (data gets infographics, stories get photos, quotes get typography); a design process that fits your resources including batch design sessions, template-first approach, and approval workflow; a visual accessibility checklist covering contrast ratios, alt text, font sizes, and color-blind friendly palettes; and a measurement approach for tracking visual content performance (engagement by visual type, brand recall, and share rates). Include a 30-day visual content system setup plan.

**Expected output:** A visual content strategy with identity system, template specifications, design process, and accessibility guidelines
**Pro tip:** Your visual system should work in black and white - if it does not communicate without color, the design is relying on decoration rather than structure

### 2.66 Webinar and Virtual Event Content Planner
**Use case:** Plan the full content ecosystem around webinars and virtual events from promotion through follow-up
**Best for:** demand generation teams, webinar hosts, event marketers

Act as a webinar content strategist who has managed the full content lifecycle for events generating thousands of leads. I need a complete content plan for my upcoming webinar or virtual event. My webinar topic is [topic], the target audience is [description], the date is [date], the host or speaker is [name], the format is [live/automated/hybrid], my registration goal is [number], and the primary business goal is [leads, sales, brand awareness, or education]. Design a complete webinar content ecosystem with: a promotion content calendar (14 days before) including email sequence (save the date, speaker announcement, early bird incentive, final reminder), social posts per platform (hook-focused, speaker spotlight, teaser content), and partnership promotion asks; a webinar script structure with timed segments including opening hook, agenda, educational content (70%), interactive element (polls, Q&A), offer or CTA, and closing with clear next step; a slide deck outline with slide-by-slide content and visual suggestions; a live engagement plan with poll questions, chat prompts, and Q&A management approach; a follow-up sequence (post-webinar) including thank you email with recording link, content recap (blog or LinkedIn post), content repurposing plan (clips, quotable moments, key stat graphics), lead scoring criteria based on attendance duration and engagement, and a nurture track for attendees versus no-shows versus registrants who did not attend; and a measurement framework tracking registration rate, attendance rate, engagement score, and conversion to next step.

**Expected output:** A complete webinar content ecosystem with promotion calendar, script, slides, engagement plan, and follow-up sequence
**Pro tip:** The majority of webinar conversions happen in the FOLLOW-UP, not during the event - your post-webinar email sequence is often more important than the webinar itself

### 2.67 User-Generated Content Campaign Designer
**Use case:** Design and launch UGC campaigns that get your audience creating content about your brand
**Best for:** Social media managers, brand marketers, community managers

Act as a user-generated content strategist who has launched campaigns generating millions of pieces of customer content. I need a UGC campaign that gets my audience creating and sharing content around my brand. My brand is [brand name], my product or service is [description], my audience is [description], my platforms are [platforms], my campaign goal is [social proof, brand awareness, product launches, or community building], and my incentive or motivation for participants is [discount, feature, prize, recognition, or intrinsic motivation]. Design a UGC campaign with: a campaign concept with a name, theme, and clear creative direction that makes it easy for users to participate; submission guidelines including format requirements, content rules, legal and rights considerations, and approval process; a content brief or inspiration pack showing examples of what great participation looks like in different formats (photo, video, text, review); an incentive and recognition structure for participants (featured account, product discount, prize, or community status); a moderation and curation system for reviewing submissions, handling inappropriate content, and selecting featured entries; a distribution plan for sharing the best submissions across your channels with proper attribution and permission; a legal checklist covering rights to use, attribution requirements, content ownership, and platform-specific terms; and a measurement framework tracking participation rate, submission quality, engagement on UGC versus branded content, and conversion impact. Include a 14-day campaign launch timeline.

**Expected output:** A complete UGC campaign design with concept, guidelines, incentive structure, moderation system, and legal checklist
**Pro tip:** The easiest UGC to generate is a review or testimonial - start there before attempting creative campaigns like photo contests. Reviews require the least creative effort from users and produce the most directly useful social proof

### 2.68 Content for Niche and Micro-Communities
**Use case:** Create content that resonates with small, passionate communities rather than broad audiences
**Best for:** Community-led brands, niche creators, B2B marketers in specialized industries

Act as a niche content strategist who focuses on reaching small but deeply engaged audiences in specialized communities. I need content that resonates with a specific, passionate community rather than trying to reach everyone. My brand serves [niche audience description], the community is centered around [shared interest, industry, or identity], the community gathers on [platforms: forums, Reddit, Slack, Discord, in-person], the audience size is [small to medium], their shared vocabulary and inside references include [terms and context], and my content goal is [trust, authority, or sales within this niche]. Design a niche content strategy with: a community listening process for identifying the specific questions, debates, and terminology this community uses; content formats and styles that feel native to this community (long-form forum posts, detailed how-to guides, insider analysis, collaborative documents) rather than broadcast formats; a credibility-building approach including engaging with community history, acknowledging community thought leaders, contributing before promoting, and showing genuine interest in the community beyond your commercial goals; the specific dos and dont's for content in this community based on their norms and pet peeves; a relationship-building content calendar focusing on value contribution first, with promotional content making up no more than 10% of activity; and a growth path showing how deep engagement with a small community creates more business value than shallow engagement with a large audience. Include real examples of brands that succeeded by going narrow and deep.

**Expected output:** A niche community content strategy with listening process, native formats, credibility approach, and do/dont guidelines
**Pro tip:** In a niche community, ONE piece of content that becomes the definitive resource on a topic is worth more than 100 broadly appealing posts - go deep enough to become the link everyone in the community shares

### 2.69 Content Governance and Editorial Standards Guide
**Use case:** Create editorial guidelines that maintain quality, consistency, and brand alignment across all content creators
**Best for:** Content operations managers, editors, brand managers overseeing multi-contributor content programs

Act as a content governance specialist who has built editorial standards for publishing teams and content marketing departments. I need a content governance framework that keeps quality consistent when multiple people create content for my brand. My brand is [brand name], my contributors include [in-house writers, guest authors, freelancers, AI tools, or agencies], my content types are [blog, social, video, email, downloads], my volume is [pieces per month], and my current quality challenges are [inconsistent voice, factual errors, brand misalignment, or formatting issues]. Design a content governance system with: an editorial style guide covering voice and tone, grammar and punctuation rules, formatting standards, brand terminology, and links to reference resources; a content quality checklist that every piece must pass before publishing with specific criteria for each content type; a role and responsibility matrix showing who creates, reviews, approves, and publishes each content type with sign-off requirements; an AI content policy covering when AI tools can be used, what requires human review, disclosure guidelines, and quality standards for AI-assisted content; a content lifecycle policy including creation, review, publishing, updating, archiving, and retirement with timeframes for each stage; a contributor onboarding template that walks new writers or creators through the standards in under 30 minutes; a quality audit process with a scoring rubric, audit frequency, and improvement feedback loop; and a version control and rollback process for published content. Include a one-page quick reference guide that summarizes the entire governance framework.

**Expected output:** A content governance framework with editorial style guide, quality checklist, role matrix, AI policy, and audit process
**Pro tip:** The best content governance is the kind contributors actually read - your style guide should be under 10 pages, include examples of right and wrong, and be tested on a new contributor before finalizing

### 2.70 Content Velocity and Newsjacking System
**Use case:** Create a system for producing timely, relevant content in response to breaking news and trending topics
**Best for:** News-driven brands, social media teams, growth marketers using current events

Act as a newsjacking and real-time content specialist who has helped brands capitalize on trending topics within hours. I need a system for creating fast, relevant content when news breaks in my industry. My brand is [brand name], my industry is [sector], my content platforms are [platforms], my typical approval process takes [timeframe], and my risk tolerance is [conservative/moderate/aggressive]. Design a content velocity system with: a monitoring setup including the news sources, alerts, social listening tools, and Google Trends configurations to catch relevant stories early; a news assessment framework for deciding which stories to cover using criteria like relevance to audience, alignment with brand values, timeliness window, competitive response, and risk assessment score; a rapid content creation workflow with pre-approved templates for different news response types (hot take, data add, industry context, explainer, rebuttal, or roundup) and the specific approval path for each; a tiered response system defining response times (Tier 1: same day within 4 hours for major industry news, Tier 2: next day for secondary stories, Tier 3: same week for trends); a content template library for rapid response with fill-in-the-blank structures for each platform; a risk and compliance checklist for newsjacking content covering libel, context accuracy, sensitivity, and brand reputation; a post-mortem process for reviewing what worked after each newsjacking attempt; and a content calendar integration showing how to balance planned content with real-time opportunities. Include a decision tree flowchart for choosing whether to respond to a news event.

**Expected output:** A content velocity and newsjacking system with monitoring, assessment framework, rapid workflows, and risk management
**Pro tip:** Speed matters but ACCURACY matters more - being first with wrong information damages credibility far more than being second with correct information. Always verify before publishing, no matter how fast the window

## 3. Business Operations & Strategy Prompts (50 Prompts)

### 3.1 Strategic Planning and Vision Setting
**Use case:** Develop a comprehensive business strategy and long-term vision
**Best for:** CEOs, founders, strategic planners

Act as a strategic business consultant. I need to develop a clear business strategy and vision for my company.

My company: [company name and description] | Industry: [industry] | Current stage: [startup/growth/scale/mature] | Revenue: [current revenue] | Team size: [employees] | Target market: [who you serve] | Competitors: [main competitors] | Challenges: [current obstacles] | Time horizon: [1/3/5 years]

Create a strategic plan framework. Vision Statement — Define a compelling 5-year vision that articulates where the company is going and why it matters. Mission Statement — Clarify your core purpose and what you do every day. Core Values — Identify 3-5 values that guide decision-making and culture. Strategic Pillars — Break down the vision into 3-5 major focus areas (e.g., market expansion, product innovation, operational excellence). OKRs — For each pillar, define 1-2 objectives with 3-5 measurable key results for the next quarter and year. Competitive Analysis — Use a simplified Porter's Five Forces or SWOT to identify strategic advantages. Resource Requirements — What talent, capital, and technology are needed to execute. Risk Assessment — Identify top 5 risks and mitigation strategies. Review Cadence — How often to review and adjust (quarterly recommended).

**Expected output:** Complete strategic plan with vision, pillars, OKRs, and risk assessment
**Pro tip:** A good strategy is 80% about what you WON'T do — be as clear about trade-offs as you are about goals

### 3.2 Business Model Evaluation and Design
**Use case:** Analyze, refine, or completely redesign your business model
**Best for:** Founders, entrepreneurs, business strategists

Act as a business model innovator. I need to evaluate and improve my company's business model.

Company: [describe your business] | Current model: [subscription/marketplace/SaaS/ecommerce/services/etc.] | Revenue streams: [how you make money] | Cost structure: [major costs] | Customer segments: [who pays] | Distribution channels: [how you reach them] | Key partners: [suppliers, distributors, etc.] | Market trends: [changes affecting your model] | Goals: [growth, profitability, diversification]

Conduct a business model analysis. Canvas Mapping — Document all 9 building blocks of the Business Model Canvas. Revenue Stream Analysis — Evaluate each revenue stream for profitability, scalability, and growth potential. Cost Structure Optimization — Identify 5-10 ways to reduce costs or shift from fixed to variable. Value Proposition Check — Does your model deliver unique value that customers will pay for? Distribution Efficiency — Are you reaching customers through the lowest-cost, highest-conversion channels? Scalability Assessment — Can this model grow without proportional cost increases? Model Innovation Opportunities — Suggest 3 alternative business models (e.g., go from project-based to subscription, add marketplace, introduce tiered pricing). Risk Analysis — What makes this model fragile (customer concentration, supplier dependency, regulatory risk)? Recommendations — Top 5 actions to strengthen the model.

**Expected output:** Complete business model analysis with innovation opportunities and action plan
**Pro tip:** The most dangerous business model is the one that worked yesterday — always be evolving

### 3.3 Operational Efficiency Audit
**Use case:** Identify waste and optimize business operations
**Best for:** COOs, operations managers, business owners

Act as an operational efficiency expert. I need to audit my operations and find optimization opportunities.

Department/process to audit: [specific area or "company-wide"] | Current workflow: [brief description of key processes] | Pain points: [where things slow down or break] | Team size: [number of people involved] | Tools used: [current software/tools] | Budget: [available for improvements] | Timeline: [when improvements are needed by]

Conduct a comprehensive operations audit. Process Mapping — Document current workflows step-by-step (use SIPOC or value stream mapping). Bottleneck Identification — Where do delays, rework, or handoff issues occur? Time Waste Analysis — Identify 7 wastes: defects, overproduction, waiting, non-utilized talent, transportation, inventory, motion, extra processing. Automation Opportunities — Which repetitive tasks can be automated with existing tools or affordable software? Communication Audit — Are decisions delayed by unclear ownership or excessive meetings? Tool Assessment — Are your tools integrated well or creating data silos? Span and Layer Analysis — Is your organizational structure efficient? Recommendations — For each issue: the fix, estimated effort, expected impact, and priority order. Success Metrics — How to measure improvement (cycle time, error rate, cost per unit).

**Expected output:** Operations audit with prioritized improvement recommendations
**Pro tip:** The biggest efficiency gains come from eliminating steps, not speeding them up

### 3.4 Financial Planning and Budgeting
**Use case:** Create or revise a financial plan, budget, or forecast
**Best for:** CFOs, finance teams, business owners

Act as a financial planning expert. I need to create a comprehensive financial plan or budget.

Company type: [describe business] | Revenue: [current and projected] | Costs: [fixed and variable] | Headcount: [current and planned] | Growth stage: [startup/growth/mature] | Time period: [monthly/quarterly/annual] | Goals: [profitability, growth, cash preservation] | Current challenges: [cash flow, margins, etc.]

Create a financial planning framework. Revenue Forecasting — Build bottom-up projections based on sales pipeline, historical trends, and market conditions. Expense Budgeting — Categorize all costs (COGS, payroll, marketing, R&D, G&A) with realistic assumptions. Cash Flow Management — Project cash inflows and outflows monthly; identify funding gaps. Scenario Planning — Create 3 scenarios: base case, optimistic, pessimistic with trigger points for each. KPI Dashboard — Define 10-15 key financial metrics (burn rate, runway, CAC, LTV, gross margin, EBITDA, ARR, churn). Budget Allocation — Recommend % allocation across departments (e.g., 30% engineering, 25% sales/marketing, 20% operations). Cost Optimization — Identify 10% in cost savings without impacting growth. Capital Requirements — How much funding is needed, when, and for what? Review Process — Monthly vs quarterly review cycle with variance thresholds.

**Expected output:** Complete financial plan with budgets, forecasts, KPIs, and scenario analysis
**Pro tip:** A budget is only as good as the assumptions behind it — document every assumption explicitly

### 3.5 Risk Management Framework
**Use case:** Identify, assess, and mitigate business risks
**Best for:** Risk managers, executives, business owners

Act as a risk management consultant. I need to develop a risk management framework for my business.

Company: [describe business] | Industry: [specific industry] | Size: [revenue and headcount] | Key operations: [what the business does] | Current risk approach: [none/informal/structured] | Risk appetite: [conservative/moderate/aggressive] | Regulations: [applicable regulatory requirements]

Build a comprehensive risk management framework. Risk Identification — Categorize risks: strategic, operational, financial, compliance, reputational, cybersecurity. For each category, list 5-10 specific risks. Risk Assessment — For each risk, rate likelihood (1-5) and impact (1-5) to create a risk score and prioritize. Risk Response — For each risk, choose: avoid, reduce, transfer (insurance/outsource), or accept with contingency plan. Key Risk Indicators — Define 3-5 metrics per critical risk that trigger action when thresholds are breached. Governance — Define risk ownership, review cadence, escalation path, and board reporting. Business Continuity — Create a basic continuity plan for top 3 most impactful risks. Insurance Review — Are you adequately insured for identified risks? Compliance Checklist — Applicable regulations and compliance status. Risk Register Template — Standard format to document and track all risks.

**Expected output:** Risk management framework with register, assessment, and mitigation plans
**Pro tip:** The risks that keep you up at night are rarely the ones that actually hurt you — focus on high-impact, high-likelihood risks

### 3.6 Project Management Office Setup
**Use case:** Establish PMO or improve project management practices
**Best for:** PMs, operations leads, growing companies

Act as a PMO consultant. I need to set up or improve project management practices in my organization.

Organization size: [number of employees] | Current practices: [what's working, what's not] | Team structure: [functional/matrix/dedicated] | Project types: [software, marketing, operations, etc.] | Tools: [current project tools] | Pain points: [missed deadlines, scope creep, unclear priorities] | Budget: [available if any]

Design a PMO framework. Governance Structure — Define project tiers (small/medium/large/critical) with different approval and oversight requirements. Methodology Selection — Recommend approach: agile (Scrum/Kanban), waterfall, or hybrid based on project types. Process Standardization — Create templates for: project charter, status report, risk log, change request, post-mortem. Resource Management — How to allocate people across projects, track utilization, and resolve conflicts. Prioritization Framework — Weighted scoring model to evaluate and rank projects (strategic alignment, ROI, urgency, risk). Reporting Cadence — Daily standups for teams, weekly status for stakeholders, monthly portfolio review for executives. Tool Configuration — How to set up your PM tool (Jira, Asana, Monday) for consistency. Success Metrics — On-time delivery, budget variance, stakeholder satisfaction, team satisfaction, ROI realization.

**Expected output:** Complete PMO framework with templates, governance, and metrics
**Pro tip:** The best PMO is invisible — if people notice the process more than the progress, you've over-engineered it

### 3.7 Supply Chain Optimization
**Use case:** Analyze and improve supply chain operations
**Best for:** Supply chain managers, logistics directors, manufacturers

Act as a supply chain optimization expert. I need to analyze and improve my supply chain.

Industry: [ecommerce/manufacturing/retail/etc.] | Current supply chain: [describe key flows] | Suppliers: [number and locations] | Inventory: [current approach to stock management] | Logistics: [shipping, warehousing approach] | Pain points: [delays, costs, quality issues] | Technology: [current systems used] | Goals: [cost reduction, speed, reliability]

Conduct a supply chain analysis. Mapping — Document end-to-end flow from raw materials to customer delivery. Supplier Evaluation — Rate suppliers on cost, quality, reliability, and lead time. Identify single-source risks. Inventory Analysis — Are you carrying too much (waste) or too little (stockouts)? Calculate optimal reorder points. Logistics Audit — Evaluate shipping costs, delivery times, carrier performance, and warehouse efficiency. Technology Assessment — Can automation, RFID, or supply chain software improve visibility? Risk Mitigation — Develop contingency plans for supplier failure, logistics disruption, and demand spikes. Cost Reduction Opportunities — Identify 10 areas to reduce costs (consolidation, renegotiation, alternative sourcing, route optimization). Sustainability — Opportunities to reduce carbon footprint and waste. Implementation Roadmap — Prioritize improvements by effort and impact.

**Expected output:** Supply chain analysis with cost reduction and risk mitigation recommendations
**Pro tip:** The cheapest item in your supply chain might be the most expensive when it fails — don't optimize cost at the expense of reliability

### 3.8 Partnership and Alliance Strategy
**Use case:** Develop a strategic partnership program to accelerate growth
**Best for:** Partnership managers, business development, growth teams

Act as a strategic partnership consultant. I need to develop a partnership and alliance strategy.

Company: [describe your business] | Industry: [your industry] | Target customers: [who you serve] | Current partnerships: [any existing partners] | Capabilities: [what you offer — API, integrations, co-marketing, referrals] | Goals: [lead generation, revenue, market expansion, integration] | Competitors' partners: [who they partner with]

Design a partnership strategy. Partner Types — Identify 4-5 partner categories (tech integrations, channel/resellers, strategic alliances, referral partners, complementary services). Partner Selection Criteria — Define what makes an ideal partner: audience overlap, complementary product, reputation, reach, market fit. Outreach Strategy — How to identify and approach target partners (warm introductions, events, cold outreach). Partnership Tiers — Structure partnerships by value: Tier 1 (strategic, revenue share), Tier 2 (integrations, co-marketing), Tier 3 (referral, affiliate). Agreement Templates — Create simplified partnership agreements for each tier. Enablement Materials — What partners need: sales decks, integration docs, co-branded assets, training. Success Metrics — Track: leads from partners, partner-sourced revenue, integration adoption, partner satisfaction. Management Cadence — Quarterly business reviews for Tier 1, bi-annual for Tier 2, annual for Tier 3. Program Evolution — How to scale the program from 5 to 50+ partners.

**Expected output:** Partnership strategy framework with tiers, outreach, and management approach
**Pro tip:** The best partnerships make money for BOTH sides within 90 days — if it takes longer, most partners lose interest

### 3.9 Compliance and Regulatory Management
**Use case:** Build or improve compliance programs and regulatory adherence
**Best for:** Compliance officers, legal teams, regulated businesses

Act as a compliance consultant. I need to develop or improve a compliance management program.

Industry: [finance/healthcare/tech/SaaS/etc.] | Regulations: [GDPR, HIPAA, SOC2, PCI, SOX, etc.] | Company size: [employees and reach] | Current compliance: [what exists vs nothing] | Data types handled: [customer data, PII, financial, health] | Geography: [where you operate and sell] | Budget: [available for compliance tools/personnel]

Design a compliance program. Regulatory Inventory — List all applicable regulations and requirements with compliance deadlines. Gap Analysis — Assess current state vs requirements; identify gaps and remediation priorities. Policy Framework — Create or update: data protection policy, access control, incident response, vendor management, employee training. Controls Implementation — Map required controls to specific processes, tools, and ownership. Documentation — Build audit-ready documentation: data flow maps, processing records, consent mechanisms. Training Program — Mandatory training for all employees, specialized training for data handlers. Monitoring and Auditing — Continuous monitoring tools, scheduled internal audits, external audit preparation. Incident Response — Procedure for breach detection, containment, notification, and remediation. Vendor Management — Due diligence process for all third-party data processors. Review Cycles — Annual program review, quarterly control testing, continuous monitoring.

**Expected output:** Compliance program framework with gap analysis, controls, and monitoring
**Pro tip:** Perfect compliance on paper with no operational reality is worse than no compliance — your controls must actually work

### 3.10 Remote and Hybrid Work Strategy
**Use case:** Design or optimize remote/hybrid work policies and practices
**Best for:** HR leaders, executives, operations managers

Act as a future-of-work consultant. I need to design or improve my organization's remote/hybrid work model.

Company size: [employees] | Current model: [fully remote/hybrid/office-first] | Roles: [which roles can be remote] | Location: [where your team is/needs to be] | Pain points: [communication, culture, productivity concerns] | Tools: [current collaboration stack] | Culture: [current culture strengths and challenges]

Design a remote/hybrid work strategy. Operating Model — Define clear policies: remote days required, core collaboration hours, office purpose, travel expectations. Communication Guidelines — Written vs synchronous, response time expectations, meeting culture (camera on/off, async-first). Manager Training — How to manage remote teams: trust over surveillance, output over hours, regular 1:1s, virtual watercooler. Tool Stack — Required: video conferencing, chat (Slack/Teams), project management, knowledge base, virtual whiteboard. Culture Building — Intentional practices: virtual team building, recognition programs, all-hands, random connections. Onboarding — Remote onboarding program: buddy system, week-by-week plan, equipment shipping. Performance Management — OKRs or similar objective framework, regular feedback loops, outcome-based evaluation. Wellness — Boundaries between work and life, mental health support, reasonable availability expectations. Equity — Ensure remote employees have equal access to opportunities, visibility, and advancement.

**Expected output:** Complete remote/hybrid work strategy with policies, tools, and culture programs
**Pro tip:** Remote work fails when companies try to replicate the office online instead of redesigning work for asynchronous collaboration

### 3.11 Data-Driven Decision Making Framework
**Use case:** Build systems to make decisions based on data rather than intuition
**Best for:** Executives, analytics teams, data-driven leaders

Act as a data strategy consultant. I need to build a data-driven decision-making culture and framework.

Company: [describe business] | Data maturity: [no data/some data/data-rich] | Available data: [what data sources exist] | Tools: [current analytics tools] | Key decisions: [what decisions need better data support] | Team capabilities: [data literacy level] | Challenges: [data quality, access, adoption]

Design a data-driven decision framework. Decision Inventory — Catalog major decisions made regularly and identify which lack data support. Data Infrastructure — What data needs to be collected, stored, and connected. Recommend tools based on maturity. Metrics Hierarchy — Define: North Star metric > Key Results > Leading Indicators > Lagging Indicators. Dashboard Design — Create 3 dashboards: executive (strategic KPIs), team (operational metrics), and investigative (deep dive). Analysis Playbook — Standard approach: define question, gather data, clean, analyze, visualize, decide, measure impact. Experimentation — When to run A/B tests, minimum sample sizes, decision rules for adopting changes. Data Literacy Training — Tiered program: basic (reading dashboards), intermediate (self-serve analysis), advanced (statistical methods). Governance — Data ownership, quality standards, access controls, definitions dictionary. Decision Review — Monthly process to review decisions made and whether data was used effectively.

**Expected output:** Data-driven decision framework with infrastructure, metrics, and culture plan
**Pro tip:** Perfect data that arrives too late is worthless — 80% accurate data today beats 100% accurate data next week

### 3.12 International Expansion Strategy
**Use case:** Plan and execute expansion into new geographic markets
**Best for:** CEOs, expansion leads, business development

Act as an international business consultant. I need a strategy for expanding my business into new markets.

Company: [describe business] | Current markets: [where you operate] | Target markets: [countries/regions] | Product/service: [what you sell] | Business model: [how you make money] | Resources: [budget, team available for expansion] | Motivation: [growth, diversification, demand, competition]

Create an international expansion plan. Market Prioritization — Score target markets by: market size, growth rate, competitive intensity, regulatory ease, cultural fit, operational feasibility. Market Entry Options — Evaluate: direct exporting, licensing/franchising, joint venture, wholly-owned subsidiary, acquisition. Localization Requirements — Product adaptations needed: language, currency, payment methods, cultural preferences, features. Regulatory Landscape — Entity setup, taxes, employment laws, data residency, industry-specific regulations. Go-to-Market Strategy — Localize: pricing, distribution channels, marketing messaging, sales approach, partnerships. Talent Strategy — Hire locally vs relocate vs remote. Local team structure and leadership. Financial Projections — Entry costs, timeline to breakeven, 3-year revenue and margin projections. Risk Assessment — Currency risk, political risk, cultural missteps, IP protection. Phase Plan — Start with 1 market as beachhead, prove model, then expand.

**Expected output:** International expansion strategy with market prioritization, entry plan, and risk assessment
**Pro tip:** Your first international market should be the easiest, not the biggest — prove your expansion model before tackling hard markets

### 3.13 Crisis Management and Business Continuity
**Use case:** Prepare for and manage business crises effectively
**Best for:** Executives, PR teams, operations managers

Act as a crisis management consultant. I need to develop crisis preparedness and response plans.

Company: [describe business] | Industry: [your sector] | Potential crises: [PR scandal, data breach, leadership failure, natural disaster, supply chain disruption, regulatory action] | Current readiness: [what exists vs nothing] | Stakeholders: [who needs to be communicated with] | Culture: [transparency level]

Develop a crisis management framework. Crisis Classification — Define 3-4 crisis levels with escalation criteria (Level 1: minor, handled by team; Level 2: moderate, management involved; Level 3: major, CEO/board; Level 4: existential). Crisis Team — Define roles: crisis lead, communications, legal, operations, HR, security. Pre-prepared Templates — Draft holding statements, internal communications, customer notifications, press releases, social media posts for different crisis types. Response Protocol — Step-by-step: acknowledge within 1 hour, investigate, communicate plan, execute, follow up. Communication Timeline — Internal first (within 30 min), customers (within 2 hours), public (within 4 hours), regulators (as required). Decision Framework — When to apologize vs investigate first, when to go public vs handle privately. Recovery Plan — How to restore normal operations, rebuild trust, learn from the crisis. Post-Crisis Review — Template for after-action review: what happened, what worked, what didn't, system improvements. Training and Drills — Annual tabletop exercises for top 3 crisis scenarios.

**Expected output:** Complete crisis management framework with templates, protocols, and training plan
**Pro tip:** How you handle the first hour of a crisis determines how the next month goes — speed and honesty beat perfection

### 3.14 Pricing Strategy and Optimization
**Use case:** Develop or optimize pricing models for products and services
**Best for:** Product managers, marketers, executives

Act as a pricing strategy consultant. I need to develop or optimize my pricing strategy.

Product/service: [describe what you sell] | Current pricing: [what you charge and how] | Customers: [segments and willingness to pay] | Competitors: [how they price] | Costs: [cost structure — fixed and variable] | Goals: [revenue growth, margin improvement, market share] | Market position: [premium/mid-market/budget]

Design a pricing strategy. Pricing Models — Evaluate options: cost-plus, value-based, competitor-based, dynamic, freemium, tiered, usage-based, flat-rate. Recommendation with rationale. Value Proposition — Quantify the value your product delivers. Customer WTP — Methods to gauge willingness to pay: surveys, A/B testing, Van Westendorp, conjoint analysis. Tiered Pricing Design — Create 3-4 tiers (Starter, Professional, Enterprise) with features that encourage upsell. Pricing Psychology — Charm pricing, anchoring, decoy effect, loss aversion in pricing presentation. Discounting Strategy — When and how to discount without devaluing the product. Grandfathering policy. Packaging — What features go in which tier to maximize perceived value. Competitive Positioning — Price vs competitors: premium (justify higher price), parity (compete on value), penetration (gain share). Implementation — How to change prices for existing customers: grandfather, phase in, communicate. Optimization Cadence — Annual review with quarterly adjustments.

**Expected output:** Complete pricing strategy with tiered models, psychology tactics, and implementation plan
**Pro tip:** Most companies underprice because they calculate price based on cost-plus instead of value delivered — charge for the problem you solve, not the effort to solve it

### 3.15 Vendor and Procurement Management
**Use case:** Optimize vendor selection, management, and procurement processes
**Best for:** Procurement managers, operations, finance

Act as a procurement optimization consultant. I need to improve vendor management and procurement.

Spend categories: [what you buy — software, services, materials, etc.] | Annual spend: [total procurement budget] | Number of vendors: [active vendors] | Current process: [ad-hoc/spreadsheet/automated] | Pain points: [overspend, maverick buying, poor vendor performance] | Industry: [your sector]

Design a procurement management system. Vendor Classification — Segment vendors by spend and criticality (strategic, operational, tactical, commodity). Sourcing Process — Standard RFI/RFP/RFQ process with evaluation criteria and scoring matrix. Vendor Selection Criteria — Define weighted criteria: cost, quality, reliability, service, innovation, sustainability. Contract Management — Key clauses to include: SLAs, termination terms, pricing escalators, data protection, IP ownership. Vendor Performance Management — Quarterly scorecards: uptime, response time, quality, compliance, value. Quarterly business reviews for strategic vendors. Procurement Technology — Evaluate e-procurement, spend management, and contract lifecycle tools. Maverick Buying Prevention — Approval workflows, preferred vendor lists, purchasing policies. Renewal Management — 90-day renewal calendar, negotiation timeline, competitive bids every 2-3 years. Cost Optimization Targets — 5-10% year-over-year savings targets with identified initiatives.

**Expected output:** Procurement management system with vendor segmentation, selection, and performance tracking
**Pro tip:** The most expensive vendor is rarely the highest-priced one — the one that fails to deliver on time costs far more than any premium

### 3.16 Quality Management System
**Use case:** Build or improve quality assurance and management processes
**Best for:** Quality managers, operations, manufacturing

Act as a quality management consultant. I need to build or improve a quality management system (QMS).

Industry: [manufacturing/software/healthcare/services] | Current quality approach: [none/informal/ISO certified] | Pain points: [defects, customer complaints, rework] | Standards required: [ISO 9001, Six Sigma, etc.] | Scope: [single department or organization-wide] | Team: [quality team size and capabilities]

Design a quality management system. Quality Policy — Document commitment to quality with measurable objectives. Process Documentation — Standard operating procedures (SOPs) for all critical processes. Quality Metrics — Define: defect rate, first-pass yield, customer complaints, rework cost, On-Time Delivery, audit findings. Inspection and Testing — What to check, how often, sample sizes, acceptance criteria. Corrective and Preventive Action (CAPA) — Structured process: identify problem, root cause analysis, implement fix, verify effectiveness.
